Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Introducing Qustas al-Afkar and its Author
Bibliographic front matter: title and author

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author and title of Qustas al-Afkar and explain the significance of the term 'qustas' as a criterion for logical reasoning.

Core Idea
The title 'Qustas al-Afkar' signals a 'balance' for evaluating thoughts by logical standards.

Before diving into the logical content of this course, we must first recognize the work itself. Qustas al-Afkar fi al-Mantiq (The Criterion of Thoughts on Logic) by Shams al-Din al-Samarqandi is a foundational textbook in the Islamic logic tradition. Understanding its title and author context prepares you to engage with the logical tools that follow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the title and author in Arabic
Look at the Arabic passage. The title 'قسطاس الأفكار في المنطق' appears first, then the author 'شمس الدين السمرقندي'. Notice the structure: the work's name followed by the author's name, a common bibliographic convention.
The Persian word before the author's name (شمس الدين السمرقندي) is not part of the Arabic title.
2
Parse the meaning of 'Qustas al-Afkar'
'قسطاس' (qustas) means 'balance' or 'criterion', and 'الأفكار' (al-afkar) means 'thoughts'. So the title translates to 'The Criterion of Thoughts'. This indicates the book's purpose: to provide a standard for evaluating reasoning.
The word 'قسطاس' is derived from the Greek 'kriterion' (criterion) via Syriac, showing the influence of Greek logic on Islamic scholarship.
3
Connect to the broader logic tradition
Al-Samarqandi's work is a commentary on the standard logic curriculum, often based on the Isaghuji (a summary of Aristotelian logic). This title page tells us the work belongs to the logical tradition (al-mantiq). Recognizing this helps classify the content you will study.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسطاس الأفكار في المنطق شمس الدين السمرقندي
The Criterion of Thoughts on Logic by Shams al-Din al-Samarqandi
Source pages p. 4

Commentary
This passage is the title page of the work 'Qustas al-Afkar fi al-Mantiq' (The Criterion of Thoughts on Logic) by the scholar Shams al-Din al-Samarqandi. It identifies the author and the subject matter. The word 'Qustas' (قسطاس) means 'balance' or 'criterion', and 'al-Afkar' (الأفكار) means 'thoughts'. Al-Samarqandi was a 13th-century Persian logician, astronomer, and theologian. This work is a commentary on logic, likely following the tradition of the 'Isaghuji' and other standard texts.

Key Terms
قسطاس
الأفكار
المنطق
شمس الدين السمرقندي

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Criterion or balance
C) Science
D) Thought

Key Takeaway
The title 'Qustas al-Afkar' indicates that the work provides a 'criterion' for evaluating thoughts according to logical rules.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Navigating Qustas al-Afkar: Structure and Significance
Table of contents listing the book's structure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to outline the two-part structure of Qustas al-Afkar and match each chapter to its article.

Core Idea
The fihris reveals the classical division of logic into tasawwur (concept) and tasdiq (assent).

A table of contents is more than a list—it is a roadmap of the author's pedagogical strategy. Al-Samarqandi's fihris shows that logic proceeds from simple terms to compound propositions, mirroring the very process of reasoning. In this lesson, you will learn to read this roadmap and understand why the book is structured as it is.

Guided Path
1
Identify the major divisions
Look at the first-level headings: Introduction, First Article, Second Article. Notice that the introduction has two chapters on the essence and subject matter of logic.
2
List the chapters of the First Article
The First Article has ten chapters covering topics from indication of words to definitions and descriptions. These all relate to acquiring concepts (tasawwur).
Chapter 4 is about division of universals, and chapters 5–9 cover the five universals (genus, species, differentia, property, common accident).
3
List the chapters of the Second Article
The Second Article has one gate with three chapters on propositions (qadaya): their divisions, formulation, and particularity/universality/restriction. These relate to acquiring assents (tasdiq).
The term 'gate' (bab) is a sub-division within the article.
4
Observe the progression
The order moves from simple terms (words, universals) to complex statements (propositions). This reflects the logical order: first you must grasp concepts, then you can form judgments.
This progression is standard in classical logic works and mirrors the structure of arguments in kalam and fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The Sermon
Introduction.
Chapter One: On the Essence of Logic and the Need for It.
Chapter Two: On the Subject Matter of Logic.
First Article: On Acquiring Concepts
Chapter One: On the Indication of Words.
Chapter Two: On the Universal and Particular.

Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage is a table of contents (fihris) that outlines the structure of the book 'Qustas al-Afkar' by al-Samarqandi. It begins with a sermon (khuṭbah) and an introduction (muqaddimah). The introduction has two chapters: the first on the essence of logic and the need for it, the second on the subject matter of logic. Then the book is divided into two articles (maqālah). The first article deals with acquiring concepts (tasawwurāt) and consists of ten chapters covering topics from indication of words to definitions and descriptions. The second article is on acquiring assents (taṣdīqāt) and is organized under a single gate (bāb) with three chapters on propositions. The structure reflects the classical division of logic into concept and assent, as well as the progression from simple terms to compound propositions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fihris of Qustas al-Afkar, which article covers the topic of definitions?
A) First Article
B) Second Article
C) Introduction
D) None

Key Takeaway
The fihris of Qustas al-Afkar shows the logical progression from concepts to assents, which is the fundamental division in Islamic logic.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Using the fihris, determine which article covers 'Genus' and which covers 'Divisions of Propositions'. Then explain why genus belongs to concepts and propositions to assents.
?
Given a new topic, say 'The Definition of Qiyas (Analogy)', predict which article and chapter it would appear in, based on the progression shown in the fihris.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
10 min
The Two Pillars of Logic: Concepts and Assents
Lists the complete structure of the book from introduction to indices.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two main articles (maqalat) of Qustas al-Afkar and list the chapters under each article from the table of contents.

Core Idea
The structure of Qustas al-Afkar mirrors the two fundamental tasks of logic: acquiring concepts and acquiring assents.

Before diving into the technical details of logical theory, it is crucial to understand how the book itself is organized. The table of contents serves as a roadmap: it reveals the author's pedagogical plan and the logical progression from simple elements to complex reasoning. In this lesson, you will learn to navigate the two main articles of the book and their constituent chapters, laying the groundwork for efficient study.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main articles (المقالة الأولى, المقالة الثانية)
Locate the headings that say 'المقالة الأولى: في اكتساب التصورات' and 'المقالة الثانية: في اكتساب التصديقات'. These are the two major divisions of logic: the first deals with concepts (tasawwurat) and the second with assents (tasdiqat).
This division is standard in Islamic logic, following al-Ghazali and others.
2
List the chapters under the first article
Under 'المقالة الأولى', there are ten chapters (فصول), covering topics from signification of words to definitions. Scan the table of contents and note the titles from 'الفصل الأول: في دلالة الألفاظ' through 'الفصل العاشر: في المقاصد و هو الكلام في الحدود والرسوم'.
Pay attention to the five universals (genus, species, differentia, property, common accident) which are chapters 5-9.
3
List the sections and chapters under the second article
The second article begins with 'الباب الأول: في أقسام القضايا...', then 'الباب الثاني: في القياس', and finally 'الباب الثالث: فصل في توابع القياس'. Each section has multiple chapters. Note the eleven chapters on propositions, the chapters on syllogism, and the twelve paths (مسالك) under the appendages.
The third section is technically a 'فصل' but contains twelve 'مسلك' paths, each a distinct logical method.
4
Observe the end matter (indices)
After the main content, the table lists indices of names and books and references. This shows the work is a complete treatise with scholarly apparatus.
Indices are rare in classical works but as-Samarqandi included them for utility.

Tenth Path: Definition is not acquired through demonstration.

Second Part: On error and its causes.
Index of names
Index of books
References
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage is the table of contents of Qustas al-Afkar, a work on logic (mantiq) in the Islamic tradition. It begins with a khutba (introduction) and muqaddima (preface), then proceeds to two main articles (maqalat). The first article covers the acquisition of concepts (tasawwurat), dealing with words, universals, essence, the five universals (genus, species, differentia, property, common accident), and definitions. The second article covers the acquisition of assents (tasdiqat), starting with propositions (qadaya) and their types, modalities, and logical relations (contradiction, conversion). Then it moves to syllogism (qiyas), dividing it into categorical and hypothetical forms, and includes a section on the appendages (tawabi') of syllogism, which are twelve 'paths' (masalik) covering topics such as simple vs. compound syllogism, reductio ad absurdum, analysis, induction, analogy, demonstration, classification of sciences, and the proper method of debate and fallacy. The book ends with indices of names and books and references. The structure follows the typical order of Aristotelian logic as adapted in Islamic scholarship: first concepts, then judgments/propositions, then reasoning. Students should use this table of contents as a map to navigate the work and understand the author's pedagogical plan.

الباب
الفصل
المسلك

Key Takeaway
The table of contents divides logic into two sequential domains: first concepts, then assents – a progression that structures the entire study of reasoning.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
15 min
The Twelve Paths of Logical Inquiry
Lists the complete structure of the book from introduction to indices.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to name the twelve paths (masalik) listed under the appendages of syllogism and categorize them under headings like types of syllogism, acquisition of premises, and methods of debate.

Core Idea
The twelve paths of Qustas al-Afkar are a toolkit of logical methods, from simple syllogism to debate and fallacy analysis.

The third section of the second article is a rich collection of twelve 'paths' (masalik) that extend the basic theory of syllogism into advanced topics. These paths cover a wide range: compound reasoning, argument by contradiction, how premises are obtained, induction, analogy, demonstration, the classification of sciences, and even the etiquette of debate and the sources of error. This lesson will help you map these paths and understand their place in the broader logical system.

Guided Path
1
Locate the section 'الباب الثالث: فصل في توابع القياس'
In the table of contents, find the heading 'الباب الثالث: فصل في توابع القياس' (Third Section: Chapter on appendages of syllogism). This is the umbrella under which the twelve paths fall.
The word 'توابع' means appendages or corollaries, indicating these are additional topics that build on the core syllogism.
2
Read through each of the twelve paths (المسلك الأول through الثاني عشر)
From 'المسلك الأول: القياس البسيط و المركب' to 'المسلك الثاني عشر: في البحث والمناظرة', read each title and note its subject. Group them mentally: paths 1-4 deal with types and structure of syllogisms, paths 5-6 with empirical reasoning (induction and analogy), paths 7-11 with demonstrative science and its components, and path 12 with dialectic.
Note that path 12 includes two subdivisions: etiquette of research and causes of error.
3
Identify the logical function of each path
For each path, ask: What problem does this path address? For example, path 2 (قياس الخلف) is reductio ad absurdum, a method used heavily in kalam to refute opponents. Path 5 (الاستقراء) and 6 (التمثيل) are inductive and analogical reasoning, important in fiqh for deriving rulings from principles.
Understanding the purpose of each path will help you later when you encounter them in the actual text.
4
Observe the final two subdivisions under path 12
Path 12 has two parts: 'القسم الأول: في تمهيد البحث وآدابه' (preparation and etiquette of research) and 'القسم الثاني: في الغلط و أسبابه' (error and its causes). This shows that the work ends with practical guidelines for formal debate and awareness of fallacies.
This reflects the Islamic tradition of adab al-bahth (the discipline of discussion).

Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage is the table of contents of Qustas al-Afkar, a work on logic (mantiq) in the Islamic tradition. It begins with a khutba (introduction) and muqaddima (preface), then proceeds to two main articles (maqalat). The first article covers the acquisition of concepts (tasawwurat), dealing with words, universals, essence, the five universals (genus, species, differentia, property, common accident), and definitions. The second article covers the acquisition of assents (tasdiqat), starting with propositions (qadaya) and their types, modalities, and logical relations (contradiction, conversion). Then it moves to syllogism (qiyas), dividing it into categorical and hypothetical forms, and includes a section on the appendages (tawabi') of syllogism, which are twelve 'paths' (masalik) covering topics such as simple vs. compound syllogism, reductio ad absurdum, analysis, induction, analogy, demonstration, classification of sciences, and the proper method of debate and fallacy. The book ends with indices of names and books and references. The structure follows the typical order of Aristotelian logic as adapted in Islamic scholarship: first concepts, then judgments/propositions, then reasoning. Students should use this table of contents as a map to navigate the work and understand the author's pedagogical plan.

Navigating the Structure of Qustas al-Afkar
Table of contents listing chapters of the book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to navigate the three main divisions of Qustas al-Afkar and identify the core topics covered in each.

Core Idea
The table of contents is a roadmap for mastering Islamic logic from propositions to demonstration.

The table of contents of Qustas al-Afkar reveals the logical progression of the discipline. This lesson will guide you through its architecture so you can locate any topic efficiently.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three major books
Scan the table of contents for 'الباب الأول', 'الباب الثاني', 'الباب الثالث'. These are the three main divisions: propositions, syllogism, and consequences of syllogism.
2
List the key chapters for each book
Under each book, note the chapter titles. For Book 1 (propositions), chapters 4-11 cover conversion, modality, contradiction, etc. For Book 2 (syllogism), chapters 1-2 with sections. For Book 3 (methods), 12 paths (masalik) are listed.
3
Recognize the logical progression
The order is intentional: propositions are the building blocks, syllogism combines them into arguments, and methods apply these arguments to knowledge. This mirrors how logic is studied in the Islamic tradition.
4
Locate a specific topic
For practice, find where 'الاستقراء' (induction) appears. It is listed as 'المسلك الخامس' under Book 3. This shows it is considered a method of reasoning, not a type of syllogism.

The Syllogism Section: Types and Structure
Syllogism section of the table of contents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the divisions of syllogism in Qustas al-Afkar and distinguish categorical, hypothetical, and exceptive syllogisms.

Core Idea
Syllogism is divided into categorical, hypothetical, and exceptive forms, each with distinct rules.

The table of contents for Book 2 of Qustas al-Afkar lays out the types of syllogism. This lesson focuses on understanding these divisions and how they relate to each other.

Guided Path
1
Locate Book 2 on syllogism
In the TOC, find 'الباب الثاني: في القياس'. Note the two chapters: definition and divisions.
2
Note the two divisions under Chapter 2
Chapter 2 has two sections: 'القسم الأول: في القياسات الحملية' (categorical syllogisms) and 'القسم الثاني: في الأقيسة الشرطية الافترانية' (conditional hypothetical syllogisms).
3
Identify the exceptive syllogism
After the second section, there is a sub-entry: 'القسم الثاني من القياس: القياس الاستثنائي' (exceptive syllogism). This is a further subdivision of the hypothetical syllogism.
4
Understand the progression
The order from categorical to hypothetical to exceptive reflects increasing complexity. Categorical syllogisms deal with absolute statements, hypothetical with conditional ones, and exceptive with eliminative reasoning.

The Masalik: Methods of Logical Reasoning
List of twelve masalik (paths) in the table of contents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the twelve masalik (paths) in Qustas al-Afkar and classify them into types: structural, analytical, evidential, and procedural.

Core Idea
The twelve masalik provide a comprehensive toolkit for logical reasoning beyond basic syllogisms.

Book 3 of Qustas al-Afkar contains twelve 'paths' (masalik) that apply syllogistic reasoning to various scientific and dialectical contexts. This lesson explores each path and its purpose.

Guided Path
1
List the first five masalik
Paths 1-4 cover structural aspects: simple/compound syllogism, reductio, acquiring premises, analysis. Path 5 is induction.
2
List the next four masalik (6-9)
Paths 6-9 cover evidential and scientific reasoning: analogy (6), demonstration (7), parts of sciences (8), interpenetration of sciences (9).
3
List the last three masalik (10-12)
Paths 10-12 cover procedural and dialectical topics: definition not acquired by demonstration (10), demands/objectives (11), research and disputation (12).
4
Categorize the masalik
Group them into: Structural (1-4), Evidential (5-7), Scientific classification (8-9), Procedural (10-12). This helps recall.

Introducing Key Logical Topics from Qustas
Lists key topics of logic discussed in the editor's introduction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the significance of the key logical topics listed in the editor's introduction of Qustas.

Core Idea
The editor's introduction maps the entire science of logic through its essential topics.

This passage gives us a bird's-eye view of the main topics a logician must master. Instead of diving into arguments, we first need to know the terrain. Each term represents a foundational concept that will be unpacked in later lessons.

Guided Path
1
Locate each Arabic term
Read through the Arabic passage and identify each distinct term: مبحث تصورات, موضوع منطق, شبهة مجهول مطلق, مباحث دلالت, كلي طبيعي, جنس مقولات, فصل, تعريف.
2
Match terms to translations
For each Arabic term, find its English equivalent from the translation provided: Topic of Concepts, Subject of Logic, The Problem of the Absolutely Unknown, Topics of Signification, Natural Universal, Genus of Categories, Differentia, Definition.
3
Categorize by concept vs assent
Determine which topics belong to the realm of concepts (tasawwurat) and which to assent (tasdiq). Most here are about concepts; 'subject of logic' and 'problem of absolutely unknown' are meta-logical.
Classical logic divides into tasawwurat and tasdiq.
4
Understand the 'absolutely unknown' problem
Focus on 'شبهة مجهول مطلق'. This is a debated issue: can we know something that is completely unknown? It challenges the foundations of definition and concept formation.
This problem is often discussed to highlight the need for clear definitions.
5
Connect to typical logic manual structure
Observe how these topics appear in the standard order of logic manuals: first signification, then concepts, universals, categories, differentia, definition. This ordering is deliberate.
Understanding the order helps navigate later lessons.

Commentary
This passage presents a list of topics from the editor's introduction to the critical edition of Qustas. These include foundational issues in logic: the study of concepts (tasawwurat), the subject matter of logic, a discussion of the 'absolutely unknown' (majhul mutlaq), topics of signification (dalala), the natural universal (kulli tabi'i), the genus of categories (jins al-maqulat), differentia (fasl), and definition (ta'rif). These are standard topics in the opening sections of logic manuals.

Introduction and Front Matter

Navigating the Structure of an Islamic Logic Textbook: The Case of Qustas al-Afkar
Table of contents listing chapters and influences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to parse the table of contents of an Islamic logic work to identify its major sections and the logical progression from concepts to arguments.

Core Idea
The table of contents is your roadmap: it shows the logical flow from simple ideas to complex proofs.

The table of contents you have before you is the skeleton of Qustas al-Afkar. It tells you not only what is in the book, but the order in which logical skills are developed. By learning to read this map, you will be able to navigate any classical logic text with ease.

Guided Path
1
Find the two main divisions
Look for the headings 'مبحث تصورات' (Concepts) and 'مبحث تصديقات' (Assents). These are the two pillars of the book.
Concepts come first because you need simple ideas before you can combine them into propositions.
2
Examine the subsections under concepts
Notice topics like signification, four relations, natural universal, differentia, and definition. They build from basic to complex.
3
Examine the subsections under assents
Here you find propositions (affirmative, negative, quantified, etc.), conversion, contradiction, and then syllogism (definition, divisions, corollaries).
This section moves from simple statements to compound arguments.
4
Identify the list of influences
The final part lists earlier philosophers like Aristotle, al-Farabi, and al-Ghazali. This shows the tradition Samarqandi builds upon.
Recognizing these influences helps situate the text in the broader intellectual history.

Commentary
This passage is the table of contents of the book 'Qustas al-Afkar' by Shams al-Din al-Samarqandi, as presented in the modern editor's introduction. It outlines the structure of the work, beginning with biographical and bibliographical sections on Samarqandi himself, then proceeding to the main logical content. The core of the book is divided into two major parts: 'Mabahith al-Tasawwurat' (Section on Concepts) and 'Mabahith al-Tasdiqat' (Section on Assents). Under concepts, it covers topics such as the subject of logic, signification, the four relations, universals, categories, differentia, and definition. Under assents, it deals with propositions (affirmative, negative, conditional, etc.), conversion, contraposition, and then syllogism (definition, divisions, corollaries). The table also lists influences on Samarqandi from earlier thinkers, showing the Persian and Greek philosophical heritage he drew upon. This front matter serves to orient the reader to the organization of the text before entering the detailed logical discussions.

The Architecture of Qustas al-Afkar: From Concepts to Syllogism
Table of contents listing sections of Qustas al-Afkar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to map the major sections of Qustas al-Afkar and explain the logical progression from concepts to syllogisms.

Core Idea
The table of contents reveals a logical curriculum: concepts first, then definitions, propositions, contradiction, and finally syllogisms.

The editor's table of contents provides a roadmap for the entire work. It begins with basic building blocks (concepts, definitions) and advances to complex reasoning (propositions, contradiction, syllogisms). Understanding this progression helps you see the pedagogical logic behind the book.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main sections
Scan the table of contents and list the primary headings: مبحث تصورات (concepts), مبحث تعريف (definition), مبحث قضايا (propositions), مبحث تناقض (contradiction), مبحث قياس (syllogism).
2
Order them logically
Why does the book start with concepts and end with syllogism? Concepts are the simplest units; definitions combine concepts; propositions combine definitions; contradiction relates propositions; syllogisms combine propositions to yield new knowledge.
This order reflects the standard Islamic logic curriculum.
3
Note sub-topics
Under each main heading, identify key sub-topics, e.g., under propositions: positive, negative, deviant, natural, quantified, external/essential/mental propositions, modality, contradiction, conversion.
These subdivisions show the comprehensive treatment of each topic.
4
Reflect on the purpose of the title
The title 'قسطاس الأفكار' means 'balance of thoughts'. This structured progression from simple to complex provides a balanced, methodical approach to reasoning.
The structure itself embodies the idea of a 'criterion' for correct thinking.

Commentary
This passage is a detailed table of contents from the editor's introduction to the critical edition of Qustas al-Afkar. It outlines the book's major sections: On Concepts, On Definition, On Propositions, On Contradiction, On Syllogism, along with sub-topics like conversion and conditional propositions. Importantly, it also lists the intellectual influences on the author, Samarqandi, both predecessors and successors. The list includes key figures in the Aristotelian and Islamic logical tradition: Xenocrates, Aristotle, Ptolemy, Themistius, Porphyry, al-Farabi, Abu al-Barakat al-Baghdadi, al-Ghazali, and later scholars like Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, Nasir al-Din al-Tusi, and even the Latin philosopher Walter Burley. This shows the breadth of Samarqandi's sources and the transmission of logic across cultures. The table of contents also references editorial issues, such as different editions and errors. The text is in Persian, indicating the editor's language. This passage serves as a roadmap for the book and a testament to the interconnectedness of the logical tradition.

Key Terms
قسطاس (Qustas): The title of the work, meaning 'balance' or 'criterion', indicating its purpose as a standard for logical reasoning. [Note: No significant shift.]
سمرقندی (Samarqandi): The author of Qustas al-Afkar, a 13th-century logician typically identified as Shams al-Din Muhammad ibn Ashraf al-Samarqandi. [Note: There are multiple scholars with the nisba 'Samarqandi'; this refers to the logician.]

The Intellectual Network of Samarqandi: Tracing Influences
List of scholars influencing and influenced by Samarqandi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify key predecessors and successors listed in the table of contents and situate Samarqandi within the broader Islamic logical tradition.

Core Idea
Samarqandi's logical synthesis builds on a chain of thinkers from Aristotle to al-Tusi and extends to Latin scholars like Walter Burley.

The editor's table of contents is more than a list of chapters; it includes a detailed chronicle of scholars who influenced Samarqandi and those he influenced. This reveals the global transmission of logic from ancient Greece to the Islamic world and into Latin Europe.

Guided Path
1
Extract the lists of predecessors and successors
In the table of contents, locate 'تاثیر پذیری سمرقندی از پیشینیان' (Influence on Samarqandi from predecessors) and 'تاثیر گذاری بر پسینیان' (Influence on successors). List all names under each.
Predecessors include Aristotle, al-Farabi, al-Ghazali, etc. Successors include Walter Burley, Qutb al-Razi, etc.
2
Group by intellectual tradition
Classify each scholar: Greek (Aristotle, Themistius, Porphyry), Islamic (al-Farabi, al-Ghazali, al-Tusi, etc.), and Latin (Walter Burley).
This shows Samarqandi's extensive sources across civilizations.
3
Identify cross-cultural connections
Notice the presence of Latin philosopher Walter Burley (ولتر برلي) among successors. This indicates that Samarqandi's work reached beyond the Islamic world to Europe.
Such connections are rare and highlight the historical importance of this text.
4
Assess the significance of the lists
Why does Samarqandi (or the editor) include these lists? They establish intellectual authority, show the development of ideas, and demonstrate the interconnectedness of logical traditions.
This practice is common in Islamic scholarly works to show chains of transmission (isnad) but here applied to ideas.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Navigating the Logical Structure of Qustas al-Afkar
Lists chapters and sections of the book's first part.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to navigate the table of contents of Qustas al-Afkar to locate specific logical topics and understand the progression of its arguments.

Core Idea
The table of contents is a structured roadmap guiding the reader from introductory topics to detailed analysis of universals and definitions.

The table of contents of Qustas al-Afkar is not just a list of chapters; it is a carefully designed intellectual itinerary. By understanding its structure, you will see how al-Katibi systematically moves from the essence of logic, through the acquisition of concepts, to the detailed study of the five universals. This lesson will train you to use this roadmap effectively.

Guided Path
1
Locate the main divisions
Identify the sermon (khuṭba), introduction (muqaddima), and the two treatises. Note that the first treatise is on acquiring concepts, and the second (implied) is on judgments.
2
Trace the progression within chapters
In Chapter One of the first treatise, the focus is on the indication of words – the building block of logic. Next, Chapter Two treats the universal and particular, essential predication, etc. This order reflects the movement from language to concepts.
3
Identify key logical terms in the headings
Look for terms like 'part prior to the whole' (differentia) and 'part posterior to the whole' (species). These are key to understanding definition theory.
4
Map the structure to the standard Islamic logic curriculum
Compare this table with other logic texts: typically, after preliminaries, they cover words (alfāẓ), then universals (kulliyāt), then definitions (ḥudūd), then propositions and syllogisms. Qustas follows a similar pattern.

المبحث الثاني: حمل المواطأة و حمل الاشتقاق

تنبيه
المبحث الرابع: الكلّي الطبيعي و المنطقي و العقلي

Commentary
This passage is the table of contents (fihrist) of the book Qustas al-Afkar by Najm al-Din al-Katibi, a renowned work on logic. It begins with a sermon (khatba) and introduction (muqaddima), followed by a detailed index. The contents are organized into chapters (fasl) and investigations (mabhath). The first chapter discusses the essence of logic and the need for it, while the second covers the subject matter of logic. The first treatise focuses on acquiring concepts (tasawwurat), starting with the indication of words, dividing utterances into single and compound, and further into noun, verb, and particle. It then treats the universal and particular, including essential and derivative predication, and the triple division of the universal (natural, logical, mental). Next, essence and its parts are examined, distinguishing between essential and accidental, and clarifying the term 'essential' in works other than Porphyry's Isagoge. The final chapters cover the division of the five universals and a detailed study of genus, its definition, and its role in constituting species.

Key Terms
الخطبة (al-khuṭba): The introductory sermon of the book, often containing praise of God and the purpose of the work.
المقدمة (al-muqaddima): The introduction to the book, setting the stage for the study of logic.
الفصل (al-faṣl): A chapter of the book, a major division covering a broad topic.
المبحث (al-mabḥath): An investigation or subsection within a chapter, focusing on a specific aspect.
الجزء المتقدم على الكل (al-juzʾ al-mutaqaddim ʿalā al-kull): The part that is logically prior to the whole, such as genus is prior to species.
الجزء المتأخر عن الكل (al-juzʾ al-mutaʾakhkhir ʿan al-kull): The part that is posterior to the whole, such as differentia is posterior to species.
الذاتي (al-dhātī): Essential property that constitutes the essence of a thing, as opposed to accidental. [Note: In later logic, 'essential' is often distinguished from 'accidental' in definitions.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

The table of contents of Qustas al-Afkar is not a mere index but a structured introduction to the science of logic, demonstrating the logical order of topics from language to universals to definitions.

The Structure of Qustas al-Afkar: Navigating the Table of Contents
Listing chapters and sections of the book's two main articles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to navigate the chapter structure of Qustas al-Afkar and identify its main divisions.

Core Idea
The table of contents is a map of the logical journey from concepts to assents.

In any systematic work of Islamic logic, the table of contents is not just a list—it is a roadmap of the order of learning. Qustas al-Afkar, like many madrasa texts, is divided into two main articles: the first on acquiring concepts (tasawwurat) and the second on acquiring assents (tasdiqat). The chapters under each article follow a logical progression. By mastering this map, you will be able to navigate the entire text and understand how each part fits into the whole.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main articles
Look at the overall structure: the text mentions 'المقالة الأولى' (first article) and presumably a second article. Although the second article is not detailed in this excerpt, recognize that the book is divided into two major parts.
The second article typically covers propositions and syllogisms, but is not shown here.
2
List the chapters of the first article
From the table of contents, find all the 'الفصل' headings under the first article. They are: chapter on the essence of logic, chapter on signification, universal/particular, essence/parts, division of universals, genus, species, differentia, property, general accident, and purposes (definitions).
There are 10 chapters in the first article.
3
Note the sections within each chapter
Each chapter has multiple 'المبحث' sections. For example, chapter 2 has five sections. Recognizing this granularity helps locate specific topics.
Sections are numbered but not all have titles shown.
4
Locate the key terms from the index
Find where 'الماهية' and 'الكليات الخمسة' appear. This prepares you for the conceptual content.
These terms appear in chapters 1 and 4 respectively.

The division into chapters (fusul) and sections (mabahith) reflects the systematic approach of Islamic logic. Introduction and Front Matter

The Two-Part Structure of Qustas al-Afkar
Table of contents with two main articles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two main divisions of logic in Qustas al-Afkar (tasawwur and tasdiq) and locate which chapters belong to each article.

Core Idea
The logical curriculum is built on two pillars: conceptualization (tasawwur) and assent (tasdiq).

The table of contents of Qustas al-Afkar reveals the overarching structure of the book. Just as a building has two floors, so this logical work is divided into two major articles (maqalat). Understanding this division helps you immediately see what the author considers the fundamental parts of logic.

Guided Path
1
Locate the two main articles (maqalat)
Scan the table for the word 'المقالة' (maqala). You will find 'المقالة الأولى' (implied) and 'المقالة الثانية: في اكتساب التصديقات'. Note that the first article deals with tasawwur (conceptualization) although it is not explicitly named here; the second article explicitly deals with tasdiq (assent).
The first article is not labeled in this chunk, but its chapters cover definitions and universals, which are the domain of tasawwur.
2
Identify the chapters of the first article
Look at the chapters (فصول) before the second article. They range from 'الفصل السادس: في النوع' to 'الفصل العاشر: في المقاصد' (definitions and descriptions). These belong to the first article.
Chapters One through Five are not listed in this chunk but are assumed to exist.
3
Identify the chapters of the second article
After 'المقالة الثانية: في اكتساب التصديقات', you see 'الباب الأول: في أقسام القضايا...' and then chapters from 'الفصل الأول' to 'الفصل الحادي عشر'. These all deal with propositions, conversions, contradictions, and conditionals.
This article focuses on the tools for acquiring assent through correct reasoning.
4
Confirm the logical progression
Notice that the book moves from simple concepts (species, genus, differentia) to complex judgments (propositions, syllogisms). This mirrors the classical order: tasawwur precedes tasdiq.

Commentary
This passage is the table of contents of the book Qustas al-Afkar fi al-Mantiq. It displays the hierarchical structure of the work, beginning with the title and then listing the chapters (fusul) and investigations (mabahith). The book is divided into two main articles (maqalat): the first article deals with tasawwur (concepts) covering the five universals, definition, and the like; the second article deals with tasdiq (assent) focusing on propositions, their conversions, contradictions, and conditionals. The numerous numbers interspersed in the text are likely page references to the original printed edition, though many appear corrupted in the OCR. This outline serves as a roadmap for the reader, showing the organization of topics from basic logical terms to complex conditional syllogisms.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
7 min
Navigating the Logical Topics through the Table of Contents
Table of contents detailing hierarchical structure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to parse the hierarchical structure (maqala, bab, fasl, mabhath) of Qustas al-Afkar and identify the sequence of topics within the first article.

Core Idea
A table of contents is a map: learning its legend lets you navigate the logical terrain.

The table of contents of Qustas al-Afkar uses a clear hierarchy: articles (maqalat), sections (abwab), chapters (fusul), and investigations (mabahith). By learning to read this structure, you can quickly locate where the author discusses any given topic, from the five universals to conditional syllogisms.

Guided Path
1
Identify the highest level: articles (maqalat)
Find the word 'المقالة' in the passage. You will see 'المقالة الثانية' explicitly. The first article is not labeled but is everything before that marker.
In printed books, 'المقالة الأولى' may appear on a separate page not included in this chunk.
2
Identify the section level (bab) within the second article
After 'المقالة الثانية', look for 'الباب الأول: في أقسام القضايا...'. This is the only bab shown in the table of contents. It groups the first eleven chapters.
Not all maqalat necessarily contain abwab; the first article seems to skip the bab level.
3
Identify chapters (fusul) and their number
Chapters are marked by 'الفصل' followed by a number. In the first article, we have chapters six through ten. In the second article, chapters one through eleven under the bab. List them in order.
Chapters one through five of the first article are missing from this chunk, likely on an earlier page.
4
Identify investigations (mabahith) within chapters
Within each chapter, look for 'المبحث' followed by a number. For example, in 'الفصل السادس: في النوع', there are three investigations: definition of species, ranks of species, and specifying the species that is one of the five universals.
Some chapters have only one mabhath; others have multiple. This level gives the most granular topic.

Commentary
This passage is the table of contents of the book Qustas al-Afkar fi al-Mantiq. It displays the hierarchical structure of the work, beginning with the title and then listing the chapters (fusul) and investigations (mabahith). The book is divided into two main articles (maqalat): the first article deals with tasawwur (concepts) covering the five universals, definition, and the like; the second article deals with tasdiq (assent) focusing on propositions, their conversions, contradictions, and conditionals. The numerous numbers interspersed in the text are likely page references to the original printed edition, though many appear corrupted in the OCR. This outline serves as a roadmap for the reader, showing the organization of topics from basic logical terms to complex conditional syllogisms.

مقالة
باب
فصل
مبحث

Checkpoint
What is the first investigation (mabhath) listed under Chapter Six (في النوع)?
A) في مراتب النوع
B) تعريف النوع
C) في تعيين النوع الذي أحد الكليات الخمسة
D) في الفصل المقوم و المقسم

Key Takeaway
The table of contents uses a consistent four-level hierarchy (article, section, chapter, investigation) that builds from broadest to most specific topic, mirroring the logical progression of the book.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Using the table of contents, list the full hierarchical path (from maqala down to mabhath) for the topic 'تعريف الخاصة' (definition of property).
?
Identify which chapter contains the investigation 'في المقولات' (on the categories). Is it part of the first or second article? Explain.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
10 min
Overall Structure of Qustas al-Afkar
Detailed table of contents of the book

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace the two-part structure of Qustas al-Afkar and identify the main divisions of each part.

Core Idea
Qustas al-Afkar progresses from propositions to syllogisms, mirroring the logical journey from simple concepts to complex reasoning.

Before diving into detailed logical theories, it is crucial to understand the map of the book. Qustas al-Afkar is divided into two major parts: first, the study of propositions (qadaya) which includes types, modality, conversions, contradictions, and conditionals; second, the study of syllogisms (qiyas) covering categorical, conditional, and mixed forms. This lesson will help you navigate the book and see how each topic builds on the previous one.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main parts
Look at the beginning of the table of contents. The book is divided into two parts: the first part deals with propositions (القضايا) and the second with syllogisms (القياس). Note how these correspond to the two fundamental building blocks of logic: terms combined into propositions, and propositions combined into syllogisms.
2
Skim part one's chapters
Observe the chapters in the first part: modality, negation, contradiction, conversion, and conditionals. These are all topics that refine and transform propositions in preparation for syllogistic reasoning.
3
Skim part two's divisions
The second part begins with categorical syllogisms and their figures, then moves to conditional syllogisms (conjunctive and disjunctive), and finally to composite syllogisms and derivations. Notice the increasing complexity.
4
Note the inclusion of al-Farabi's views
The table mentions a conclusion on 'Conversion and Syllogisms according to al-Farabi', showing that the author engages with the Islamic philosophical tradition, not just Greek logic.

First Path: On deriving categorical from two conjunctives: in syllogism composed of two conjunctives and the sharing in a complete part of them and incomplete. 539.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is the detailed table of contents of 'Qustas al-Afkar fi al-Mantiq' (The Just Scale of Thoughts in Logic). It provides a comprehensive outline of the book's structure, covering two main parts: the first part (not fully shown) deals with propositions (qadaya) including their types, conversions, contradictions, and conditionals; the second part deals with syllogisms (qiyas), including categorical and conditional syllogisms, their figures, mixes, and various compositions. The author organizes the material into chapters (fusuul), topics (mabaahith), sections (aqsaam), and paths (masaarik). Notable topics include the distinction between external (kharijiyya), real (haqiqiyya), and mental (dhihniyya) propositions, the conditions for productive syllogistic figures, and the works of al-Farabi on conversion and syllogisms. This table of contents serves as a navigational tool for the reader, showing the logical progression from basic propositional logic to complex syllogistic theory.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
10 min
Navigating the Fihrist: The Structure of Qustas al-Afkar
Author presents the detailed table of contents for the book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to parse the hierarchical structure of the fihrist (table of contents) and locate specific logical topics within the book Qustas al-Afkar.

Core Idea
The fihrist is a roadmap: it reveals the logical progression from definitions of syllogism to its types and applications.

The table of contents (fihrist) is not mere listing — it is a blueprint of the author’s logical system. In this lesson, you will learn to navigate the fihrist of Qustas al-Afkar, identifying the major divisions (chapters, sections, investigations, courses) and understanding how they relate to each other. This skill is essential for efficient study of any classical Islamic logic text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main chapters (abwab)
The fihrist begins with 'الباب الثاني: في القياس' (Chapter Two: On Syllogism). Notice that the first chapter is not included in this excerpt. This tells us that the book likely starts with introductory material (e.g., on terms and propositions) before reaching syllogisms.
Keep in mind that the fihrist is selective; it may not show all chapters.
2
Recognize the hierarchy of headings
The fihrist uses a nested structure: fasl (section), qism (division), mabhath (investigation), maslak (course). For example, under الباب الثاني we find الفصلان, then فصول, then أقسام, etc. This hierarchy reflects the logical decomposition of the subject.
Often, the hierarchy is indicated by indentation or numbering (e.g., 1.1, 1.2).
3
Locate the two main divisions of syllogism
Under الفصل الثاني (On Divisions of Syllogism), there are three major qisms: القسم الأول: في القياسات الحملية (categorical), القسم الثاني: في الأقيسة الشرطية الاقترانية (conditional conjunctive), and later القسم الثاني من القياس: القياس الاستثنائي (exceptive). This shows the author's classification of syllogisms.
The exceptive syllogism is listed after the conditional conjunctive sections.
4
Observe the detailed sub-sections within conditional syllogisms
The conditional conjunctive division is further broken down into compositions of two conditionals, two disjunctives, categorical with conditional, etc., each with multiple 'courses' (masalik). These classifications are based on the nature of the connecting term (middle) and the type of propositions.
The complexity shows how thorough the author is.
5
Identify the appendices and special topics
After the syllogism sections, the fihrist lists: الباب الثالث (Chapter 3) on appendices, including simple/compound syllogism, reductio, induction, analogy, demonstration, parts of sciences, dialectic, and fallacies. This reveals the broader scope of the book beyond basic syllogisms.
The last part on error and fallacies shows practical application.

Second Course: Of Conditional and Disjunctive: The Middle is a Non-Complete Part. Third Course: Of Conditional and Disjunctive: The Middle is a Complete Part of One and Non-Complete of the Other. Third Course: On Deducing Categoricals from Two Disjunctives and Sharing in a Complete Part and Non-Complete. Fourth Course: On Deducing Categoricals from Two Disjunctives and Sharing in a Non-Complete Part Only. Fifth Course: On Deducing Categoricals from Conditional and Disjunctive and Sharing in a Complete Part and Non-Complete. Sixth Course: On Deducing Categoricals from Conditional and Disjunctive and Sharing in a Non-Complete Part. Seventh Course: On Deducing Categoricals from Categorical and Conditional. Eighth Course: On Deducing Categoricals from Categorical and Disjunctive. Second Part: Deducing Conditionals from Categorical Syllogisms. Warning. Note: Composition of Conditional Syllogisms. Second Course: On Syllogism of Reductio ad Absurdum. Third Course: On Acquiring Premises. Fourth Course: On Analysis. Fifth Course: Induction. Sixth Course: Analogy. Seventh Course: On Demonstration. Eighth Course: On Parts of Sciences. Ninth Course: On Overlap, Proportion, and Distinction of Sciences. Tenth Course: The Definition is Not Acquired by Demonstration. Eleventh Course: On Objectives. Commentary
This passage is the detailed table of contents (fihrist) of the book 'Qustas al-Afkar fi al-Mantiq' by an author. It outlines the structure of the entire work, organized into chapters (bab), sections (fasl), divisions (qism), investigations (mabhath), courses (maslak), etc. The second chapter is on syllogism (qiyas), which is subdivided into categorical and conditional syllogisms, covering definitions, figures, mixtures, and various types. Later sections cover topics like demonstration, induction, analogy, dialectic, and fallacies. This fihrist serves as a roadmap for the reader, indicating the logical progression from basic concepts to advanced applications.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

The Two Kingdoms and Their Paths
Detailed table of contents listing sections on syllogisms, definitions, and dialectics.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major divisions (kingdoms) and sections (paths) in the table of contents of Qustas al-Afkar and describe their logical focus.

Core Idea
The table of contents is the logical map of the entire text.

This lesson examines the first part of the detailed table of contents of Qustas al-Afkar, which lists the kingdoms and their paths. The second kingdom deals with deriving categorical syllogisms from conditional and disjunctive premises, while the third kingdom continues with more complex combinations. Understanding this structure helps you navigate the book's logical arguments.

Guided Path
1
Locate the second kingdom (الملك الثاني)
Find the line that begins with 'الملك الثاني' and note its topic: deriving categoricals from two conditionals.
The second kingdom focuses on categorical conclusions from conditional premises.
2
Count the paths under the second kingdom
Scan for 'المسلك الرابع' onwards; the second kingdom includes paths 4 through 8, each specifying a different combination of conditional premises.
Paths 4-8 are all within the second kingdom.
3
Identify the third kingdom (الملك الثالث)
Find the line 'الملك الثالث' and see that it deals with deriving categoricals from two disjunctives, with perfect and imperfect parts.
The third kingdom extends the derivation to disjunctive premises.
4
Find the transition to conditional syllogisms
After the paths, locate 'القسم الثاني: استنتاج الشرطية من الأقيسة الحملية', which shifts to deriving conditionals from categoricals.
This marks a move from categorical conclusions to conditional conclusions.

Qustas al-Afkar fi al-Mantiq

The second kingdom on deriving categorical syllogisms from two conditionals and sharing in a part that is not perfect from them. The third kingdom: on deriving categoricals from two disjunctives and sharing in a perfect part and non-perfect from them. 543 The fourth path: on deriving categoricals from two disjunctives and sharing in a part that is only imperfect from them. The fifth path: on deriving categoricals from a conditional and a disjunctive and sharing in a perfect part and an imperfect part from them.
The sixth path: on deriving categoricals from a conditional and a disjunctive and sharing in a part that is not perfect from them.
The seventh path: on deriving a conditional from a categorical and a conditional. The eighth path: on deriving a categorical from a categorical and a disjunctive.
The second section: Deriving a conditional from categorical syllogisms.
Warning.
Correction: Composition of conditional syllogisms.
Conclusion on the syllogism of proportion.
The second part of the syllogism: The exceptional syllogism.
The third chapter: Section on the appendages of the syllogism.
The first path: The simple and compound syllogism.
The second path: On the reductio ad absurdum syllogism. The third path: On acquiring premises. The fourth path: On analysis.

Commentary
This passage is the detailed table of contents of the book Qustas al-Afkar fi al-Mantiq (The Just Balance of Thoughts in Logic). It outlines the structure of the entire work, listing major divisions called 'kingdoms' (malik) and 'paths' (maslak), as well as sections on conditional and categorical syllogisms, definition, demonstration, dialectics, and fallacies. The table shows that the book is organized into several main parts: first, deriving categorical conclusions from various conditional premises; second, deriving conditional conclusions from categorical premises; third, the exceptional syllogism; and then appendages covering simple and compound syllogisms, reductio, induction, analogy, demonstration, parts of sciences, definition, objectives, and disputation. It also includes sections on error and fallacies, followed by indices. This front matter serves as a roadmap for the reader, indicating the logical topics covered and their sequence. The page numbers listed are references to where each section begins.

From Demonstration to Disputation
Detailed table of contents listing sections on syllogisms, definitions, and dialectics.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the topics covered in the appendages (توابع القياس) and the final sections on investigation and fallacies as presented in the table of contents of Qustas al-Afkar.

Core Idea
The appendages transform syllogistic theory into a complete scientific method.

This lesson focuses on the latter part of the table of contents, which begins with 'توابع القياس' (appendages of the syllogism). These sections cover advanced topics such as simple and compound syllogisms, reductio, induction, analogy, demonstration, the structure of sciences, definition, and the art of disputation. The final sections deal with dialectical investigation and fallacies, completing the logical curriculum.

Guided Path
1
Locate the section 'توابع القياس'
Find the line 'الباب الثالث: فصل في توابع القياس' and note that it is the third chapter after the exceptional syllogism.
This section contains paths 1 through 12.
2
List the first eight paths
From 'المسلك الأول: القياس البسيط و المركب' to 'المسلك الثامن في أجزاء العلوم'. Identify each topic.
These cover foundational logical methods.
3
List paths nine to twelve
Paths nine to twelve cover interrelation of sciences, definition, objectives, and disputation.
Note that path ten states 'definition is not acquired through demonstration'.
4
Identify the dialectics and fallacies sections
After path twelve, locate 'القسم الأول: في تمهيد البحث وآدابه' and 'القسم الثاني: في الغلط وأسبابه'.
The fallacies section includes examples (أمثلة للمغالطات).

The Collaborative Network Behind the Edition of Qustas
Author expresses gratitude to collaborators for the edition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key contributors to the edition of Qustas and explain how each contributed to the study of Samarqandi's logic.

Core Idea
A scholarly edition is a collaborative effort relying on a network of experts and institutions.

This acknowledgments section reveals the scholarly community that made the critical edition of Qustas possible. Understanding this network helps you appreciate how knowledge is transmitted and refined over time. Notice that the contributions range from manuscript provision to thesis supervision, each playing a vital role in producing a reliable text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central figure and his project
The edition revolves around Shams al-Din Samarqandi's logical works, especially his innovations in conditional syllogisms. Look for the term 'Shams al-Din Samarqandi' and notice the focus on 'shartiyyat' (conditionals).
2
List the contributors and their gifts
Each person named provided a specific resource: Khaled al-Ruwayhab shared information; Seyyed Hossein Mousavian provided a dissertation; Ali Asghar Jafari Valani supervised theses; students edited sections; others gave manuscripts or feedback. Categorize them as providers of information, manuscripts, supervision, or editorial review.
There are 11 items in the list.
3
Note the geographic and institutional spread
Contributors come from Harvard, University of Tehran, Shahid Motahari University, Turkish libraries, and the Research Institute of Wisdom and Philosophy in Iran. This shows the international collaboration in Islamic logic studies.
4
Assess the impact on the final edition
Without these contributions, the edition would lack key manuscripts, editorial guidance, and specialized knowledge. Each acknowledgment points to a critical need that was filled.
Consider how missing any one would weaken the edition.

سپاس گزاری

تصحیح و تحقیق این کتاب با یاری بسیاری از دوستان و همکاران به انجام رسیده است. در اینجا لازم میبینیم از همه عزیزانی که هر یک به گونه ای در به انجام رسیدن این کتاب سهم داشته اند
سپاس گزاری کنم

۱ نخستین آشنایی من با شمس الدین سمرقندی از طریق دوست و همکار گرامی خالد الرويهب از دانشگاه هاروارد بود. او در ایمیلی به تاریخ ۶ تیر ۱۳۸۹ (۲۷) ژوئن ۲۰۱۰م.) به من اطلاع داد که سمرقندی در مباحث شرطیات نوآوریهای چندی دارد. با این راهنمایی دو نسخه کتابخانه مجلس شورای اسلامی از شرح القسطاس را از سایت کتابخانه مجلس دانلود کردم و با مطالعه آن به اهمیت نوآوری های منطقی سمرقندی پی بردم حاصل این مطالعات نشر نوآوریهای سمرقندی در مباحث شرطیات در وبلاگ منطق در ایران به تاریخ ۲۱ خرداد ۱۳۹۱ زیر عنوان قیاس اقترانی شرطی نزد شمس الدین سمرقندی و سپس به طور کاملتر در نشریه منطق پژوهی ۱۳۹۳ شماره ۱۰ با عنوان منطق ربط نزد شمس الدین سمرقندی و در نشریه جاویدان خرد ۱۳۹۷ ش شماره ۳۴ با عنوان «کمیت) قیاس شرطی نزد شمس الدین سمرقندی . همچنین سپاس گزاری میکنم از دوست و همکار گرامی سید حسین موسویان، که فایل رساله دکتری نجم الدین پهلوان و تصحیح او از سمرقندی را در دی ماه ۱۳۹۲ در اختیارم
گذاشت
. دوست و همکار گرامی علی اصغر جعفری ،ولنی که سفارش این جانب برای ارائه تصحیح بخشهایی از شرح القسطاس به عنوان پایان نامه ارشد دانشجویانی در دانشگاه
شهید مطهری و راهنمایی این پایان نامه ها را پذیرفتند.

۲ سپاس گزاری
. دو تن از دانشجویان دانشگاه شهید مطهری فاطمه شمسی کوشکن و سید محمد حسینی دولت آباد، که به ترتیب تصحیح بخشهای قضایا و قیاس از شرح القسطاس را به انجام
رساندند و در سالهای ۱۳۹۴ و ۱۳۹۵ از پایان نامه های خود دفاع کردند.
. هم چنین نجم الدین پهلوان که در شهریور ۱۳۹۴ نسخه چاپ شده قسطاس الأفكار راکه در ۲۰۱۴م منتشر کرده بود برایم فرستاد و بعدها دست نوشته کتابخانه فیض الله افندی از شرح القسطاس را نیز در اختیارم قرار داد.
. در این میان دوست و همکار گرامی غلامرضا دادخواه نسخه ای از تصحیح کتاب سمرقندی را با عنوان علم الآفاق و الأنفس که در سال ۲۰۱۴م. در انتشارات مزدای آمریکا منتشر کرده بود در اختیارم نهاد مقدمه تفصیلی این کتاب در باره زندگی سمرقندی و نوشته ها و اندیشه های او بعدها بسیار به کارم آمد و در مقدمه این کتاب در بخش زندگی نامه سمرقندی و آثارش از آن بهره فراوان برده ام افزون بر این، آقای دادخواه بخش تصحیح قسطاس الأفکار را در یکی از مراحل میانی از نظر گذرانده، پیشنهادهای ارزنده ای برای ارتقای کمی و کیفی آن ارائه داد. . دوست و همکار گرامی مهدی عظیمی که در دانشکده الهیات دانشگاه تهران بخش قياس شرح القسطاس را به عنوان پایان نامه ارشد به یکی از دانشجویش اشکان باقری سپردند که در سال ۱۳۹۶ از آن دفاع شد.
. استاد ارجمند حسین معصومی همدانی که راهنمایی هایش در برخی مباحث طبیعیات کتاب بسیار ارزنده بود.
. دوست گرامی احمدرضا رحیمی ریسه که افتخار آشنایی با او را به تازگی پیدا کرده ام سه دست نویس قسطاس الأفكار از کتابخانه های ترکیه ایاصوفیه و عاطف افندی را سخاوتمندانه در اختیارم نهادند که در تصحیح این کتاب از دو مورد از آن سه بهره بردم. .۱۰ دوست و همکار گرامی و معاونت محترم پژوهشی موسسه حکمت و فلسفه سید محمود یوسف ثانی که برخی خطاهای نگارشی را گوشزد کردند و پیشنهادهایی برای ارتقای نصحیح پیشنهاد نمودند.
.۱۱ در پایان از مسؤولان مؤسسه پژوهشی حکمت و فلسفه ایران سپاس گزارم که با حمایت مادی و معنوی از این اثر، امکان نشر آن را فراهم ساختند.
Acknowledgments

The correction and research of this book have been accomplished with the help of many friends and colleagues. Here I deem it necessary to thank all the dear ones who each in their own way have contributed to the completion of this book.

1. My first acquaintance with Shams al-Din Samarqandi was through the dear friend and colleague Khaled al-Ruwayhab from Harvard University. In an email dated 27 June 2010, he informed me that Samarqandi has several innovations in the topics of conditionals. With this guidance, I downloaded two copies from the Islamic Consultative Assembly Library of the Sharh al-Qustas from the library's website, and upon studying it, I realized the importance of Samarqandi's logical innovations. The result of these studies was the publication of Samarqandi's innovations in the topics of conditionals on the blog 'Logic in Iran' on 11 June 2012 under the title 'Conditional Conjunctive Syllogism according to Shams al-Din Samarqandi', and then more completely in the journal Logic Research in 2014, issue 10, with the title 'Relevant Logic according to Shams al-Din Samarqandi', and in the journal Javedan Kherad in 2018, issue 34, with the title 'The Quantity of Conditional Syllogism according to Shams al-Din Samarqandi'. I also thank the dear friend and colleague Seyyed Hossein Mousavian, who provided me with the file of Najm al-Din Pahlavan's doctoral dissertation and his edition of Samarqandi in January 2014.

. The dear friend and colleague Ali Asghar Jafari Valani, who accepted my request to present the edition of parts of the Sharh al-Qustas as master's theses for students at Shahid Motahari University and supervised these theses.

2. Acknowledgments: Two students from Shahid Motahari University, Fatemeh Shamsi Kushkan and Seyyed Mohammad Hosseini Dolatabad, who respectively accomplished the edition of the sections on propositions and syllogism from the Sharh al-Qustas and defended their theses in 2015 and 2016.

. Also Najm al-Din Pahlavan, who in September 2015 sent me the printed edition of Qustas al-Afkar, published in 2014, and later provided me with the manuscript from the Fayzullah Efendi Library of the Sharh al-Qustas.

. Meanwhile, the dear friend and colleague Gholamreza Dadkhah provided me with an edition of Samarqandi's book titled 'Alam al-Afaq wa al-Anfus', published in 2014 by Mazda Publishers in America. The detailed introduction of this book about the life of Samarqandi and his writings and thoughts later proved very useful to me, and I have made extensive use of it in the introduction of this book in the section on Samarqandi's biography and works. Moreover, Mr. Dadkhah reviewed the edition of Qustas al-Afkar in one of its intermediate stages and offered valuable suggestions for its quantitative and qualitative improvement.

. The dear friend and colleague Mehdi Azimi from the Faculty of Theology of the University of Tehran assigned the section on syllogism of the Sharh al-Qustas as a master's thesis to one of his students, Ashkan Bagheri, who defended it in 2017.

. The esteemed professor Hossein Ma'soumi Hamedani, whose guidance in some topics of physics in the book was very valuable.

. The dear friend Ahmadreza Rahimiyan Rise, whom I have recently had the honor of meeting, generously provided me with three manuscripts of Qustas al-Afkar from Turkish libraries, Ayasofya and Atif Efendi, of which I used two in the edition of this book.

.10. The dear friend and colleague, and the respected research deputy of the Institute of Wisdom and Philosophy, Seyyed Mahmoud Yosuf Thani, who pointed out some writing errors and suggested improvements for the edition.

.11. Finally, I thank the officials of the Research Institute of Wisdom and Philosophy of Iran, who provided the means for publishing this work through material and spiritual support.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is the acknowledgments section of the edition of Qustas. The author expresses gratitude to numerous individuals and institutions that contributed to the research and production of the book. The section begins with a general thanks to all who helped. Then, in a numbered list, the author details each contributor: first, Khaled al-Ruwayhab, who introduced the author to Samarqandi's work on conditionals; second, Seyyed Hossein Mousavian, who provided a doctoral dissertation and edition; third, Ali Asghar Jafari Valani, who supervised theses on the Sharh al-Qustas; fourth, two students who edited sections on propositions and syllogism; fifth, Najm al-Din Pahlavan, who provided printed and manuscript copies; sixth, Gholamreza Dadkhah, who offered an edition of another work and reviewed the present edition; seventh, Mehdi Azimi, who supervised a thesis on the syllogism section; eighth, Hossein Ma'soumi Hamedani, who advised on physics topics; ninth, Ahmadreza Rahimiyan Rise, who supplied manuscripts from Turkish libraries; tenth, Seyyed Mahmoud Yousuf Thani, who pointed out errors and suggested improvements; and eleventh, the Research Institute of Wisdom and Philosophy, for their support. This front matter does not contain logical content but situates the book within a scholarly network.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Identifying the Correct Title of Qustas al-Afkar
Editor discusses incorrect titles and surveys editions and studies of Qustas al-Afkar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct title of Shams al-Din al-Samarqandi's logical work and distinguish it from incorrect titles mentioned in secondary sources.

Core Idea
The correct title of Samarqandi's logical masterpiece is Qustas al-Afkar fi Tahqiq al-Asrar, not the misnomers found in some references.

Before studying any classical Islamic text, it is crucial to establish its correct title and authorship. In this preface, the editor of Qustas al-Afkar corrects several misattributions and surveys the scholarly work done on the text. Understanding this bibliographical groundwork ensures you engage with the right material and avoid confusion.

Guided Path
1
Locate the correct title
Find the full Arabic title in the opening line: 'قسطاس الأفكار في تحقيق الأسرار'. This is the established correct title.
The title means 'The Balance of Thoughts in Investigating Secrets'.
2
Identify the incorrect titles
The editor lists three incorrect names: 'الفسطاط', 'قسطاس الميزان', and 'القسطاس في المنطق'. Note each one.
These errors appear in some later sources.
3
Understand why they are incorrect
The editor states they are all mistaken without giving detailed reasons, but the correct title is well-attested in manuscripts.
In manuscript studies, priority is given to the title used by the author or earliest witnesses.
4
Trace the printing history
The editor mentions a Calcutta edition by Sprenger (1854) and modern studies. This shows how the text has been transmitted.
Not all editions are reliable; the editor notes errors in Pahlawan's edition.
5
Assess the current state of research
The editor lists recent theses that edited parts of the work. This tells you which sections are available in critical editions.
Knowing this helps you find the best resources for your study.

نجم الدین پهلوان این کتاب را به عنوان رساله دکتری در دانشگاه آنکارا در ترکیه در سال ۲۰۱۰م. تحقیق و به زبان ترکی ترجمه و شرح کرده است. او در سال ۲۰۱۴م این کتاب را با ویرایشی نو و البته با خطاهای فراوان منتشر کرده است که به این خطاها در بخش جداگانه ای اشاره خواهیم کرد. ما در پانوشتهای تصحیح خود به اختلاف نسخ تصحیح پهلوان با تصحیح خویش اشاره کرده ایم. پس از پهلوان علی احمد اسماعیل محمد در سال ۲۰۱۵م در گروه فلسفه اسلامی دانشگاه قاهره (دانشکده دار العلوم قسطاس الأفكار را با راهنمایی عبد الراضی محمد عبد المحسن به عنوان پایان نامه کارشناسی ارشد تحقیق کرده است با تأسف اطلاعاتی بیش از این درباره این تحقیق به دست ما نرسید. آنچه یافته ایم در پیوند زیر است که مربوط میشود به مرکزی به نام «اتحاد مكتبات الجامعات المصرية (Egyptian Universities Libraries)

Editor's preface: For this book, other names like 'al-Fustat', 'Qustas al-Mizan', or 'al-Qustas fi al-Mantiq' have been mentioned in some sources, all of which are incorrect. Edward Van Dyck in his book 'Ikhtifa' al-Qanu' bima Huwa Matbu'' as previously mentioned names Shams al-Din Samarqandi and his book 'Qustas al-Mizan' and notes that Aloys Sprenger (1813-1893) printed this book in 1854 in Calcutta, India. Nicholas Rescher also mentions this printing. The author's many attempts to find this print never succeeded. Najm al-Din Pahlawan researched this book as a doctoral dissertation at Ankara University in Turkey in 2010 and translated and commented on it in Turkish. In 2014 he published the book with a new edition but with many errors, which we will point out in a separate section. In our correction footnotes we have indicated the differences between Pahlawan's edition and our own. After Pahlawan, Ali Ahmad Isma'il Muhammad in 2015 in the Department of Islamic Philosophy at Cairo University (Faculty of Dar al-Ulum) researched Qustas al-Afkar under the supervision of Abd al-Radi Muhammad Abd al-Muhsin as a master's thesis. Unfortunately, we did not receive more information about this research. What we found is in the following link, which belongs to a center called 'Egyptian Universities Libraries'... In the Google search page under this link it says: 'Qustas al-Afkar fi al-Mantiq li Shams al-Din Muhammad ibn Ashraf al-Husayni al-Samarqandi, died 698 AH: Study and Investigation / Muhammad, Ali Ahmad Isma'il 140' which indicates the study and investigation of Ali Ahmad Isma'il. But does it mean a critical edition? We do not know. Incomplete parts of Qustas al-Afkar within parts of Sharh al-Qustas have been edited in the following master's theses in Iran: Fatima Shamsi Gushki (section on propositions, Shahid Motahhari University, 2014); Seyed Mohammad Hosseini Dolatabad (section on syllogism, Shahid Motahhari University, 2015); Ashkan Bagheri (section on syllogism, Faculty of Theology, University of Tehran, 2016).
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is from the editor's preface to the 'Qustas al-Afkar' by Shams al-Din al-Samarqandi. The editor begins by correcting the misidentification of the book's title: although some sources call it 'al-Fustat', 'Qustas al-Mizan', or 'al-Qustas fi al-Mantiq', the correct title is 'Qustas al-Afkar fi Tahqiq al-Asrar'. He then traces the printing history: Edward Van Dyck and Nicholas Rescher refer to Aloys Sprenger's 1854 Calcutta edition, which the editor could not locate. Next, he surveys modern scholarship: Najm al-Din Pahlawan's 2010 dissertation and 2014 edition (with many errors), and Ali Ahmad Isma'il Muhammad's 2015 master's thesis at Cairo University. The editor notes uncertainty about whether that thesis produced a critical edition. Finally, he lists three Iranian master's theses that edited parts of the book within commentaries: one on propositions (2014) and two on syllogism (2015 and 2016). This preface thus provides bibliographic orientation for the text.

Shams al-Din al-Samarqandi: A Key Figure in Islamic Logic
Editor's biographical introduction to Samarqandi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the main contributions of Shams al-Din al-Samarqandi to logic (mantiq) and dialectics (jadal).

Core Idea
Samarqandi's works on logic and dialectics shaped the Islamic scholarly tradition for centuries.

The editor's introduction presents Shams al-Din al-Samarqandi, an 8th/14th century scholar whose works on logic, dialectics, and kalam were widely studied. This lesson provides a biographical overview and situates him within the intellectual history of the Islamic world.

Guided Path
1
Identify Samarqandi's full name and period
Note his full name (Shams al-Din Muhammad al-Samarqandi) and approximate death date (late 8th/14th century). The passage mentions other scholars from his era.
2
List his main works on logic and dialectics
From the passage, identify works such as his commentary on Adab al-Bahth, Miftah al-Nazar, 'Ayn al-Nazar, al-Munyah wa al-Amal, and Gha'ib al-Nazar.
Some of these may be the same work under different titles.
3
Identify the commentators and glossators of his works
The passage mentions Kamal al-Din al-Shirwani as a commentator and Jalal al-Din al-Dawani as the most famous glossator. Also list others like 'Isam al-Din al-Isfarayini and 'Imad al-Din al-Kashi.
These figures show the extensive reception of Samarqandi's texts.
4
Recognize the significance of his philosophical-kalam works
The passage lists al-Saha'if al-Ilahiyya, al-Ma'arif fi Sharh al-Saha'if, al-Anwar al-Ilahiyya, etc. These works contributed to later theological debates.

Editor's introduction. About Samarqandi 11. [First edition] printed in Cairo in 1353 AH (1934 CE) edited by Mahmud al-Imam al-Mansuri, and second edition in 1435 AH (2014 CE) edited by Izza Abd al-Rahman Ahmad Abd al-Rahman al-Nadi. Muhammad bin Muhammad Khabushani; written 763 AH in Madina Dar al-Salam. Hamid al-Din al-Shashi, eighth century [AH]. Muhammad bin Shahrukh Ulugh Beg (d. 853 AH). Ala al-Din Ali bin Muhammad Shahroudi Bistami known as Musannifak (d. 875 AH). Kamal al-Din Masud Muhaqqiq al-Shirwani (d. 905 AH/1499 CE). Qutb al-Din Muhammad al-Gilani who wrote his commentary in 891 AH/1486 CE. Abd al-Latif bin Abd al-Mu'min bin Ishaq, name of the commentary Kashf al-Abkar fi 'Ilm al-Afkar. Burhan al-Din Ibrahim bin Yusuf al-Bulghari. Husayn bin Mu'in al-Din al-Yazdi al-Mibdi (d. 910 AH/1504 CE). On the commentary of Kamal al-Din al-Shirwani, many glosses have been written, and Allamah al-Dawani is the most famous glossator of this commentary. Below are the names of the glosses on this commentary and their authors briefly: Ahmad Junayd; Amir Hasan al-Rumi; Abd al-Rahim al-Shirwani; Abd al-Mu'min al-Barziti known as Nahari Zada (d. 960 AH/1456 CE); Jalal al-Din Muhammad bin As'ad al-Siddiqi al-Dawani (d. 1502/1908 CE); Isam al-Din Ibrahim bin Muhammad al-Isfarayini (died in Samarqand in 943 AH/1536 CE); Muhammad bin Abi Sa'id Taj al-Sa'idi (d. 950 AH). Ahmad Dikfuz, a scholar contemporary with Sultan Muhammad Fatih and among his courtiers. Ala al-Din Ali bin Muhammad known as Musannifak (d. 871 AH/1466 CE), date of writing: 826 AH/1423 CE. Imad al-Din Yahya bin Ahmad al-Kashi, tenth century AH, a commentary known as 'al-Hashiya al-Sawda' due to its very intricate style. [Page 27] 12 About Samarqandi. The commentary on Adab al-Bahth. Editor's Introduction. This book is a commentary on the epistle Adab al-Bahth by Ishaq bin Ibrahim al-Shashi (d. 325 AH), who is apparently the first person to write a book on the rules of discussion and debate. Miftah al-Nazar fi Sharh 'Muqaddima fi al-Jadal wa al-Khilaf wa al-Nazar' authored 690 AH. This book is a commentary on the introduction of one of the books of Burhan al-Din al-Nasafi on dialectics and debate. The next epistle is the following epistle which Walter Edward Young recently edited and published online. 'Ayn al-Nazar fi 'Ilm al-Jadal (2019 Samarqandi). Other independent books of Samarqandi in this field: al-Munyah wa al-Amal fi 'Ilm al-Jadal, Gha'ib al-Nazar fi 'Ilm al-Jadal. About these two works we do not know much, and it is even possible that they are one work or the same as the fourth. Philosophical-Kalam works: From the philosophical-kalam works of Samarqandi, the following can be mentioned: al-Saha'if al-Ilahiyya (1985 CE, Kuwait, edited by Ahmad Abd al-Rahman al-Sharif; 2007 CE, Beirut, edited by Ahmad Farid al-Mazidi); al-Ma'arif fi Sharh al-Saha'if (2015 CE, presented by Nazir Muhammad al-Nazir, translated and edited by Abdullah Muhammad Abdullah, al-Maktaba al-Azhariyya li al-Turath); al-Anwar al-Ilahiyya; Sharh al-Anwar al-Ilahiyya; Bayan Madhahib Ahl al-Sunna; Tahqiq Kalimat al-Shahada. Dadkhah 1392 p. 29.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is the editor's introduction to the book Qustas, providing a detailed biographical and bibliographical overview of the 8th/14th century scholar Shams al-Din al-Samarqandi (not to be confused with the earlier scholar Abu al-Qasim al-Samarqandi). The editor begins by noting the publication history of this edition, including the first Cairo edition (1353 AH) and a second edition (1435 AH). He then lists a chain of scholars who worked on Samarqandi's texts, such as Muhammad bin Muhammad Khabushani (who wrote in 763 AH), Hamid al-Din al-Shashi, Ulugh Beg (the Timurid ruler), and the commentator known as Musannifak. The focus shifts to the extensive commentary tradition on Samarqandi's works on logic and dialectics, particularly the commentary by Kamal al-Din al-Shirwani, which attracted many glosses (hawashi). The most famous glosses are those of Jalal al-Din al-Dawani, along with others like Isam al-Din al-Isfarayini and 'Imad al-Din al-Kashi (whose gloss is known as 'al-Hashiya al-Sawda' or the Black Gloss due to its dense style). The editor then identifies the main text being introduced: the commentary on Adab al-Bahth by Ishaq al-Shashi, who is credited as the founder of the genre of disputation theory. Other works by Samarqandi on jadal (dialectics) are listed: Miftah al-Nazar, 'Ayn al-Nazar, al-Munyah wa al-Amal, and Gha'ib al-Nazar, with a note of uncertainty about whether the last two are distinct works. Finally, Samarqandi's philosophical and kalam works are listed, including al-Saha'if al-Ilahiyya and its commentary, al-Anwar al-Ilahiyya, and treatises on Sunni doctrine and the testimony of faith. Throughout, the passage functions as a scholarly apparatus, orienting the reader to the textual history and the key figures in the reception of Samarqandi's logical and dialectical corpus.
