نسخه های قسطاس الأفکار ۷۹
مقدمة مصحح نهاية ويكون منتهى القسمة لا جائز أن يكون منقسماً إلى غير النهاية وإلا لزم انحصار ما لا يتناهى بين الحاصرين لأن ما لا يتناهى حينئذ يكون بين جانبي ذلك الجسم فحينئذ يتعين أن يكون منتهى
القسمة».
این نسخه از آغاز متن قسطاس در حدود سه سطر را فاقد است و از پایان در حدود دو هفتم متن را به طور دقیق تر تنها تا پایان مبحث قیاس اقترانی شرطی از دو منفصله (با حد وسط جزء نام در هر دو مقدمه را در بر دارد و ادامه قیاسهای اقترانی شرطی و نیز قیاس استثنانی و کل توابع القياس را حذف کرده است آخرین پاره متن در برگ ۲۰۸ از ۲۴۷ برگ نسخه واقع است. پس از این، مانند بیشتر نسخه های شرح القسطاس متن به صورت چکیده «قال ... إلى قوله ...» يا «قال ... إلى آخره» آمده است که معمولا به جای ... یک تا سه کلمه میآید با نظر به بیشتر نسخه های شرح القسطاس به نظر می رسد که این شرح به همین شیوۀ اخیر یعنی بدون متن قسطاس الأفکار و تنها با اشاره های چند کلمه ای به پارههای آن نگاشته شده و نسخه آستان قدس تا برگ ۲۰۸ به جای این اشاره های
کوتاه، پاره های متن قسطاس الأفکار را از نسخه ای که در دسترس بوده جایگزین کرده است. این نسخه از میانه سطر ششم از صفحه ۴۳ آ تا پایان صفحه ۴۳ب در واقع تکرار بخشی پیشین از کتاب است با آغاز از سه کلمۀ پایانی سطر چهاردهم از صفحه ۳۳ ب تا پایان سطر دهم از صفحه ۳۴ (ب) به نظر میرسد که این بخش تکراری در واقع دو روی یک برگ از نسخه ای بوده که نسخه آستان قدس از روی آن کتابت میشده و به اشتباه دو بار نسخه برداری شده است. اگر این احتمال درست باشد آنگاه چون این بخش مکرر دو پاره از متن قسطاس الأفکار را در میان سه پاره از متن شرح القسطاس ،دارد میتوان نتیجه گرفت که نسخه رونویسی شده اصلی نیز ترکیبی از متن و شرح قسطاس بوده است.
این نسخه اغلاط کمی دارد و در کنار متن چاپی نجم الدین پهلوان تنها منبع تصحيح حاضر بوده است. از آنجا که متن چاپی ،پهلوان چنان که نشان دادیم خطاهای فراوانی داشت این نسخه در تصحیح مهمترین نقش را ایفا کرده است؛ هر چند برای دو هفتم پایانی و مفقود متن در این نسخه تنها منبع ما متن چاپی پهلوان بوده و تنها به کمک شرح القسطاس و برداشتهای خویش تصحیح را انجام داده ایم هر چند نیم نگاهی نیز به نسخه بدلهای یاد شده در پانوشتهای پهلوان داشته ایم. از آنجا که میزان دقت و امانت پهلوان در ثبت نسخه بدلها برای نگارنده معلوم نشده است، اعتماد چندانی به آنها نکرده ایم.

۸۰ نسخه های قسطاس الأفكار
مقدمة مصحح
۲ نسخه مجلس شورای اسلامی به شماره ۳۸۵۹، دارای خط نسخ، ۳۷۱ صفحه صفحات ٢٥ سطری
این نسخه خوش خط و متأخر اما بسیار مغلوط است به گواهی اشتراکات فراوان در کاستی ها و فزونی ها نسبت به دیگر نسخه ها این نسخه به احتمال بسیار از نسخه آستان قدس رونویسی شده با نیای هر دو به یک نسخه میرسد برگ نخست این نسخه نیز افتاده است و به جای آن با خط و کاغذ دیگری، مقدمة شرح القسطاس (بدون مقدمة قسطاس (الأفكار) در یک صفحه کتابت و به نسخه افزوده شده است ،بنابراین آغاز این نسخه را باید صفحه ۲ دانست که با این عبارت آغاز میشود قال و هو مرتب على مقدّمة ومقالتين: الأولى في التصوّرات و الثانية في التصديقات. أقول: ...... شگفت اینکه پایان این نسخه همان پایان نسخه آستان قدس است جز اینکه سطر پایانی این نسخه در آن نیامده است:
پایان «المغالطة الثامنة: في أخذ ما بالقوة مكان ما بالفعل: الجزء الذي لا يتجزى موجود لأن الجسم إما أن يكون منقسماً إلى غير النهاية بأن ننصفه و ننصف نصفه و تنصف نصف نصفه لا إلى نهاية و يكون منتهى القسمة. لا جائز أن يكون منقسماً إلى غير النهاية وإلا لزم انحصار ما لا يتناهى بين الحاصرين لأن ما لا يتناهى».
با مقایسه معلوم میشود که عبارت حينئذ يكون بين جانبي ذلك الجسم فحينئذ يتعين أن يكون منتهی القسمة» که در پایان نسخه آستان قدس هست در پایان نسخه مجلس نیست. نکته دیگر اینکه پایان نسخه مجلس سطر هشتم از صفحه ۳۷۱ آن است و پایین صفحه سفید مانده است. از اینجا می توان حدس زد که نسخه رونویسی شده نسخه مجلس مانند نسخه آستان قدس تا همین قسمت را داشته است. آیا این نشان میدهد که نسخه مجلس از نسخه آستان قدس رونویسی شده است؟ با مراجعه به متن تکراری در نسخه آستان قدس میبینیم که این تکرار در نسخه مجلس نیست و از این رو احتمال رونویسی از آن نسخه که در بالا به آن اشاره شد از میان میرود ناگزیر باید این دو
نسخه را برگرفته از یک نسخه دیگر دانست که اطلاعاتی از آن در دست نیست.
به دلیل خطاهای بسیار زیاد این نسخه از مقابله متن با آن پرهیز کردیم.
نسخه ایاصوفیا به شماره ۲٥٦٥ دارای خط نسخ ٦٤ ،برگ صفحات ۲۵ سطری (با) گونه نوشت (ص)
نسخة كتابخانه ایاصوفیا با شماره ٢٥٦٥ مجموعه ای از دو کتاب سمرقندی به نامهای الصحائف الإلهية (در) علم (كلام و قسطاس الأفكار في المنطق است که اولی در برگه های اب ۱۸۶ با تاریخ
Copies of Qustas al-Afkar 79
Editor's introduction: The end, and it becomes the limit of division, it is not possible for it to be divided infinitely, otherwise it would necessitate the confinement of the infinite between two boundaries, because the infinite would then be between the two sides of that body, so then it is determined that it is the limit of division.
This copy lacks about three lines from the beginning of the text of Qustas, and from the end about two-sevenths of the text, more precisely it contains only up to the end of the topic of conditional conjunctive syllogism from two disjunctives (with the middle term being part of the name in both premises), and it omits the continuation of conditional conjunctive syllogisms as well as the exceptive syllogism and all appendices of the syllogism. The last piece of text is on folio 208 of 247 folios of the copy. After this, like most copies of Sharh al-Qustas, the text comes in summary form as 'he said ... up to his saying ...' or 'he said ... to the end', where usually one to three words replace the ellipsis. Considering most copies of Sharh al-Qustas, it appears that this commentary was written in this latter manner, i.e., without the text of Qustas al-Afkar and only with brief indications of its passages, and the Astan Quds copy up to folio 208 replaced these brief indications with passages of the text of Qustas al-Afkar from a copy that was available. This copy from the middle of line six of page 43a to the end of page 43b is actually a repetition of a previous part of the book, starting from the last three words of line fourteen of page 33b to the end of line ten of page 34b. It seems that this repeated section was actually two sides of a folio from the copy from which the Astan Quds copy was being transcribed, and it was copied twice by mistake. If this probability is correct, then because this repeated section contains two passages of the text of Qustas al-Afkar among three passages of the text of Sharh al-Qustas, it can be concluded that the original copied copy was also a combination of the text and commentary of Qustas.
This copy has few errors, and alongside the printed text of Najm al-Din Pahlavan, it has been the only source for the present edition. Since the printed text of Pahlavan, as we have shown, had many errors, this copy has played the most important role in the edition; although for the final two-sevenths and the missing text in this copy, our only source was the printed text of Pahlavan, and we carried out the edition only with the help of Sharh al-Qustas and our own judgments, although we also took a glance at the variant readings mentioned in Pahlavan's footnotes. Since the degree of Pahlavan's accuracy and reliability in recording variant readings is not known to the author, we have not relied on them much.

[PAGE_095]
80 Copies of Qustas al-Afkar
Editor's introduction
2 Copy of the Islamic Consultative Assembly, number 3859, in naskh script, 371 pages, 25 lines per page.
This copy is calligraphic and recent but highly erroneous, as evidenced by many shared lacunae and additions compared to other copies. This copy most likely was transcribed from the Astan Quds copy, with both sharing a common ancestor. The first folio of this copy is also missing, and replaced with a different hand and paper containing the introduction of Sharh al-Qustas (without the introduction of Qustas al-Afkar) written on one page and added to the copy. Therefore, the beginning of this copy should be considered page 2, which starts with the phrase: 'He said: It is arranged on an introduction and two treatises: the first on concepts, and the second on assents. I say: ......' Strangely, the end of this copy is the same as the end of the Astan Quds copy, except that the last line of this copy does not appear in it:
The end: 'The eighth fallacy: taking potential as actual: The indivisible part exists because the body is either divisible infinitely by halving it and halving its half and halving the half of its half endlessly, and there is a limit to division. It is not possible for it to be divided infinitely, otherwise it would necessitate the confinement of the infinite between two boundaries, because the infinite...'
By comparison, it becomes clear that the phrase 'then it is between the two sides of that body, then it is determined that it is the limit of division' that appears at the end of the Astan Quds copy is not at the end of the Majlis copy. Another point is that the end of the Majlis copy is line eight of page 371, and the bottom of the page is left blank. From this, it can be guessed that the transcribed copy of the Majlis copy, like the Astan Quds copy, had up to this part. Does this indicate that the Majlis copy was transcribed from the Astan Quds copy? By referring to the repeated text in the Astan Quds copy, we see that this repetition is not present in the Majlis copy, and therefore the possibility of transcription from that copy mentioned above disappears. Consequently, these two copies must be considered derived from another copy of which no information exists.
Due to the many errors of this copy, we refrained from collating the text with it.
Copy of Ayasofia, number 2565, in naskh script, 64 folios, 25 lines per page (with a variant writing).
The copy of the Ayasofia library, number 2565, is a collection of two books by Samarqandi: al-Saha'if al-Ilahiyya (on the science of Kalam) and Qustas al-Afkar on logic. The first is in folios 1-86 with the date...
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is the editor's introduction describing the manuscript sources used for the critical edition of Qustas al-Afkar. The editor first discusses the Astan Quds manuscript, noting that its beginning is missing about three lines and its end omits about two-sevenths of the text, specifically breaking off at the end of the section on conditional conjunctive syllogisms from two disjunctives. The editor explains that after that point, the manuscript, like many others of Sharh al-Qustas, provides only summarized references to the text rather than the full text. However, the Astan Quds manuscript up to folio 208 replaced these summaries with actual passages from Qustas taken from another available copy. The editor also identifies a duplicated section in this manuscript resulting from a folio error during transcription. The editor concludes that the original exemplar was a composite of text and commentary. The editor then assesses the Astan Quds manuscript as having few errors and being the most important source for the edition, supplementing the missing parts with Pahlavan's printed edition and the commentary. On page 95, the editor describes another manuscript from the Majlis Library, noting its clean script but many errors, and suggests it derives from a common ancestor with the Astan Quds manuscript. The editor compares their endings and notes the absence of the duplicate section in the Majlis copy. Finally, a third manuscript from Ayasofia is briefly mentioned as a collection of two works.

Key Takeaway
The value of a manuscript for critical edition depends on its completeness, accuracy, and genealogical relationship to other witnesses.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
10 min
Reading a Manuscript List: The Transmission of Qustas al-Afkar
Lists manuscripts and marginal notes of Qustas al-Afkar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key elements of a manuscript list and interpret marginal notes to trace scholarly engagement with a logical text.

Core Idea
Manuscript margins preserve a living debate among logicians across generations.

This passage from a modern edition lists the known manuscripts of Athir al-Din al-Abhari's Qustas al-Afkar, along with marginal notes by later scholars such as al-Katibi, al-Samarqandi, and al-Hilli. Learning to read such lists allows you to understand how texts were transmitted and how scholars engaged with each other's ideas long after the author's death. This skill is essential for verifying sources and appreciating the depth of the Islamic logical tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main text and its author
The passage begins by naming Qustas al-Afkar and references the editor's introduction. Determine that the work is by Athir al-Din al-Abhari, a prominent logician and theologian.
The work is a treatise on logic (mantiq).
2
Locate the marginal notes and their authors
Scan the Arabic for phrases like 'فائدة' (benefit), 'أجاب عنه' (he answered), or 'قال' (he said). These introduce marginal comments. Note the scholars mentioned: Ibn Kamuna, al-Bahrani, al-Katibi, al-Samarqandi, etc.
Each marginal note is attributed to a specific scholar, showing active debate.
3
Analyze the content of a sample marginal note
The first note discusses a logical point: the middle term not being repeated. Break down the logical terminology: الصغرى (minor premise), الكبرى (major premise), الوسط (middle term). Understand the technical issue about predicate and subject composition.
This note addresses a condition for a valid syllogism.
4
Compare the dates and locations of manuscripts
The list includes dates ranging from 683 AH to 862 AH and locations from Istanbul to India. Notice which manuscripts are oldest and which have known scribes.
The oldest manuscript (683 AH) is in Ayasofya Library, only a few decades after al-Abhari's death.
5
Interpret the significance of the transmission
Reflect that the multiple copies and marginal notes indicate the text was widely studied and debated. The references to scholars like 'Allama al-Hilli show the text's integration into later Islamic intellectual history.
This is evidence of the living tradition of logic in Islam.

This passage is a modern editor's introduction listing the manuscript copies of Qustas al-Afkar by Athir al-Din al-Abhari. Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
Critical Edition Methodology from Qustas al-Afkar
Editor introduces manuscripts and editorial process

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate a critical editor's choices in selecting and collating manuscript witnesses using the introduction to Qustas al-Afkar as a case study.

Core Idea
Textual criticism is a rigorous tool for establishing reliable texts in Islamic sciences.

This lesson examines the editor's introduction to Qustas al-Afkar, where he lists known manuscripts and explains his editorial process. Although not a logic lesson, the editor's method mirrors the critical thinking required in Islamic scholarship: assessing sources, rejecting unreliable ones, and seeking corroboration. You will learn to apply similar scrutiny to textual evidence in your own studies.

Guided Path
1
Inventory the manuscript witnesses
Read the list of 18 manuscripts and note their locations, dates, scribes, and number of folios. This is the raw data of the textual tradition.
The editor compiled this list from personal access, correspondence, and published catalogues.
2
Identify the initial pool of sources
The editor began with three copies: Astan Quds (low-quality images), Majlis (high-quality images but many errors), and the Pahlavan printed edition. Note his immediate rejection of the Majlis copy due to textual errors.
This shows that image quality does not compensate for textual unreliability.
3
Trace the process of collation
After initial work with two copies, the editor obtained three Turkish manuscripts. He decided to collate only two (Ayasofya 2565 and Atif Efendi 1673), rejecting the third Atif Efendi 1674 because it was undated and had multiple scribes, resembling another copy.
The editor prioritizes dated, single-scribe copies and avoids redundant witnesses.
4
Examine the use of abbreviations
The editor assigns abbreviations (ق, ص, ع for manuscripts, پ for printed edition) used in footnotes. This standardizes references across the critical apparatus.
A clear system of sigla is essential for scholarly transparency.
5
Assess the overall methodology
The editor's choices are guided by principles: prioritize older dated copies, avoid those with many errors, collate multiple witnesses to resolve discrepancies, and document all decisions. This is a model of source-critical reasoning.
These principles parallel the methods of hadith criticism (al-jarh wa al-ta'dil).

خوشبختانه پس از مقابله و تصحیح اولیه به کمک دو نسخه قدس و پهلوان به لطف دوست گرامی آقای احمدرضا رحیمی ،ریسه به سه دست نویس از کتابخانه های ترکیه ایاصوفیا ۲۵۶۵) و عاطف افندی ۱۶۷۳ و ۱۶۷۴) دسترسی پیدا کردیم که مقابله با دو نسخه ایاصوفیا ۲۵۶۵ و عاطف افندی ۱۶۷۳ را در دستور کار قرار دادیم و از آنجا که نسخۀ عاطف افندی ۱۶۷۴ فاقد تاریخ کتابت بود و گویا دو یا چند نویسنده آن را استنساخ کرده بودند و در موارد بسیاری به نسخه ایاصوفیا شباهت داشت از مقابله و تصحیح آن پرهیز کردیم.

Copies Used
Manuscript Copies
At the beginning of the work, we had only three copies: first, the manuscript of Astan Quds (no. 10650) with very low-quality images but relatively acceptable text; second, Majlis (no. 3859) with very high-quality images and relatively good handwriting but unfortunately with many textual errors; and third, the printed edition of Pahlavan. We set aside the Majlis copy from the beginning due to its very numerous errors and worked with the other two copies. In many cases we were forced to refer to the manuscripts of Sharh al-Qustas as well, although the expressions of the text and commentary sometimes became very close and in some cases were exactly identical, and in other cases they diverged, and at times the text and commentary did not correspond, and this issue made the work of collation and correction difficult.
Fortunately, after initial collation and correction with the help of the Quds and Pahlavan copies, thanks to the gracious friend Mr. Ahmad Reza Rahimy, we gained access to three manuscripts from Turkish libraries: Ayasofya 2565, Atif Efendi 1673 and 1674. We proceeded to collate the two copies Ayasofya 2565 and Atif Efendi 1673. Since the Atif Efendi 1674 copy lacked a date of copying and apparently had been transcribed by two or more scribes, and in many cases resembled the Ayasofya copy, we refrained from collating and correcting it.
In the footnotes, for the manuscripts of Astan Quds, Ayasofya, and Atif Efendi, we have used the abbreviations 'ق', 'ص', and 'ع' respectively, and for the Pahlavan edition the abbreviation 'پ'.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is the editor's introduction to the Qustas al-Afkar. It begins by listing known manuscripts of the work, giving details such as library location, call number, date of copying, scribe name, and number of folios. The list includes copies from libraries in Turkey (Ahmed III Topkapı, Atif Efendi, Manisa, Selim Agha), Iran (Astan Quds, Majlis), India (Khuda Bakhsh, Rampur), Russia (St. Petersburg), Egypt (Sabat, Dar al-Kutub al-Zahiriyya), Syria (al-Zahiriyya), and the UAE (Jum'ah al-Majid Center). The editor then describes the copies he actually used: three initial copies (Astan Quds, Majlis, and the printed Pahlavan edition), from which he discarded the Majlis copy due to many errors. Later, he obtained three Turkish manuscripts (Ayasofya 2565, Atif Efendi 1673 and 1674) and decided to collate only Ayasofya 2565 and Atif Efendi 1673, omitting Atif Efendi 1674 because it was undated and had multiple scribes. Finally, he explains the abbreviations used in the footnotes for the different sources.

مقابله (muqābala)
تصحیح (taṣḥīḥ)
مخطوط (makhtūṭ)
مقدمه مصحح (muqaddimat muṣaḥḥiḥ)

Checkpoint
According to the introduction, which manuscript did the editor set aside due to many errors?
A) Astan Quds manuscript
B) Majlis manuscript

D) Ayasofya manuscript

Key Takeaway
Critical editing requires evaluating witnesses by multiple criteria (date, scribe, error count) and collaborating with others to obtain the best sources.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Suppose you are editing a short treatise on usul al-fiqh. You have three manuscripts: one early and carefully copied, one later with many marginal notes, and one with a damaged beginning. Based on the editor's method, which two would you prioritize for collation? Justify your choice in 2-3 sentences.
?
In a hadith collection, you find two versions of a narration: one from a reliable narrator with a broken chain, and one from a less reliable narrator with a complete chain. How does the editor's treatment of the Majlis manuscript (good images but many errors) inform your approach? Write a brief analysis.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
How a Critical Edition of an Islamic Logic Text Is Prepared
Editor describes manuscripts used for critical edition of Qustas al-Afkar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the reliability of a published edition of an Islamic logical text by examining the editor's use of manuscript sources.

Core Idea
A critical edition is only as reliable as the manuscripts it collates.

This passage from the editor's introduction to Qustas al-Afkar reveals the practical challenges of establishing a stable text. The editor describes his manuscript base, explains his decisions to include or exclude copies, and shows how he navigated discrepancies between text and commentary. As serious students of Islamic logic, you need to know how to assess the textual foundation of any work you study.

Guided Path
1
Identify the editor's manuscript corpus
List all manuscripts the editor mentions: Astan Quds (10650), Majlis (3859), Pahlawan print, Ayasofya 2565, Atif Efendi 1673 and 1674. Note their origins and dates if given.
The editor initially had three copies, then accessed three more.
2
Trace the editor's criteria for inclusion
Why was the Majlis copy rejected? (Many textual errors) Why was Atif Efendi 1674 excluded? (Lacked date, multiple scribes, similar to Ayasofya) What does this tell you about editorial judgment?
The editor prioritizes textual quality over image quality.
3
Understand collation challenges
The editor had to consult Sharh al-Qustas because text and commentary overlapped or diverged. How does this affect the establishment of the text?
Interference between matn and sharh is a common textual problem.
4
Interrogate the editorial method
Does the editor explain his decisions clearly? Check if the final choice of base manuscripts (Astan Quds and Pahlawan, later Ayasofya and Atif Efendi 1673) is justified. Note the abbreviations used (ق، ص، ع، پ).
A transparent editor lists his sigla and explains his choices.
5
Apply to your own reading
When you read a modern edition of an Islamic logic text, check the introduction. Does the editor list manuscripts and explain his method? If not, the text may be less trustworthy.
This lesson equips you to judge the reliability of any critical edition.

Manuscript copy
At the beginning of the work we had only three copies: first, the manuscript of Astan Quds (number 10650) with very low quality images but relatively acceptable text; second, Majlis (number 3859) with very high quality images and relatively good handwriting, but unfortunately with many textual errors; and third, the printed copy of Pahlawan. We set aside the Majlis copy from the beginning due to its many errors and worked with the other two copies. In many cases we were compelled to also refer to manuscripts of Sharh al-Qustas, although the expressions of the text and the commentary sometimes were very close and in some cases became identical; in some cases they diverged, and at times the text and commentary did not match, making collation and correction difficult.
Fortunately, after initial collation and correction using the Quds and Pahlawan copies, thanks to dear friend Mr. Ahmadreza Rahimi, we gained access to three manuscripts from Turkish libraries: Ayasofya 2565 and Atif Efendi 1673 and 1674. We decided to collate with the two copies of Ayasofya 2565 and Atif Efendi 1673, and since the Atif Efendi 1674 copy lacked a transcription date and apparently had been copied by two or more scribes and in many cases resembled the Ayasofya copy, we refrained from collating and correcting it.
In the footnotes, for the manuscripts of Astan Quds, Ayasofya, and Atif Efendi, we used the abbreviations 'q', 's', and 'a', and for the Pahlawan print we used the abbreviation 'p'.
Images of pages from the copies used
First page of the Astan Quds manuscript number 10650
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is an editor's introduction to a critical edition of Qustas al-Afkar, a work on Islamic logic. The editor begins by listing eighteen known manuscript copies of the work, identifying them by library, shelf number, and sometimes scribe and date. He then describes the three copies initially available to him: the Astan Quds manuscript (which had low-quality images but a relatively acceptable text), the Majlis manuscript (with high-quality images but many textual errors), and the Pahlawan print edition. Due to the Majlis copy's numerous errors, he abandoned it and worked only with the Astan Quds and Pahlawan copies. The editor also had to consult manuscripts of the commentary on Qustas (Sharh al-Qustas) because the text and commentary often overlapped or diverged, complicating the collation process. Later, through the assistance of a colleague, he accessed three additional manuscripts from Turkish libraries: Ayasofya 2565 and Atif Efendi 1673 and 1674. He chose to collate the Ayasofya and Atif Efendi 1673 copies, avoiding the 1674 copy due to its uncertain origin and similarity to the Ayasofya copy. Finally, he explains the abbreviations used in the footnotes for the manuscripts: 'ق' for Astan Quds, 'ص' for Ayasofya, 'ع' for Atif Efendi, and 'پ' for the Pahlawan print. This passage serves as a methodological statement illustrating the critical approach to establishing a reliable text.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Purpose and Structure of Qustas
Author states the book's aim and its division into introduction and two articles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the purpose of the book Qustas as described by its author and outline its division into an introduction and two articles.

Core Idea
Qustas compiles the laws of logic from earlier scholars, organized into introduction, concepts, and assents.

This opening passage of Qustas reveals the author's intent and the work's architecture. Understanding this framework helps you navigate the entire logical tradition of Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Locate the author's purpose
Find the phrase 'نبدأ كتابنا جامع لقوانين المنطق' – 'We begin our book, a collection of the laws of logic.' This states the book's aim.
The author seeks to compile a comprehensive work.
2
Identify the key components of the purpose
The author mentions 'جلاء وافيا وأصولا من مقالات العلماء المتقدمين' – 'a clear exposition and principles from the articles of the earlier scholars.' Note the emphasis on clarity and prior authorities.
3
Extract the structure statement
Look for 'وهو مرتب على مقدمة ومقالدين: الأولى في الصور والثانية في التصديقات' – 'arranged into an introduction and two articles: the first on concepts and the second on assents.' This is the outline.
The two articles correspond to the two divisions of logic.
4
Verify the division
Check that the introduction is separate and the two articles are named. This is the standard division in Islamic logic.
The introduction likely covers preliminaries.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم. الحمد لله الذي خلق العقول [؟] وأدرك الحوادث [؟] والسلام على [؟] البنية القدسية والسيرة المرضية محمد وآله [؟]. وبعد: نبدأ كتابنا جامع لقوانين المنطق أردت فيه جلاء وافيا وأصولا من مقالات العلماء المتقدمين والفضلاء الماهرين مشحونة بنكات شريفة واعتراضات غريبة مشيرا إلى مواضع الخلاف ومعينا لما يوجب القبول والاحترام. [؟] وهو مرتب على مقدمة ومقالدين: الأولى في الصور والثانية في التصديقات. المقدمة [؟] فضلات الأول في [؟] المنطوري.
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah who created the intellects [?] and perceived events [?] and peace be upon [?] the holy nature and the pleasing conduct, Muhammad and his family [?]. And then: We begin our book, a collection of the laws of logic, in which I intended a clear exposition and principles from the articles of the earlier scholars and the skilled virtuous ones, filled with noble points and strange objections, pointing to points of disagreement and indicating what necessitates acceptance and respect. Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Concepts and Assents: The Two Pillars of Logic
Author states the book's aim and its division into introduction and two articles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between tasawwurat (concepts) and tasdiqat (assents) and provide an example of each from Islamic theology.

Core Idea
Logic splits into two: forming concepts and making judgments.

The Qustas begins by defining the two main parts of logic: the study of concepts (suwar/tasawwurat) and the study of assents (tasdiqat). This division is foundational for all later logical analysis in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Find the two article names
In the passage, locate 'الأولى في الصور والثانية في التصديقات'. These are the two articles.
'الصور' literally means 'forms' but here means 'concepts'.
2
Understand 'tasawwurat'
Tasawwurat are mental concepts, like definitions of terms (e.g., 'the world is created'). This part deals with simple apprehension.
We form concepts without making a truth claim.
3
Understand 'tasdiqat'
Tasdiqat are judgments of truth or falsity, such as 'the world requires a creator'. This includes propositions and syllogisms.
Assents involve commitment to truth.
4
Apply to Islamic science
Example in kalam: 'Jawhar' (substance) is a concept; 'Jawhar la yakhlu min hawadith' (substance cannot be devoid of events) is an assent.
This distinction appears in Taftazani's works.

Understanding the Author's Introduction to Qustas
Author introduces Qustas, praising God and outlining its arrangement into an introduction and two articles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the tripartite structure of Qustas and explain the author's purpose and methodological commitment.

Core Idea
A logical work's introduction reveals its author's method and scope.

In this opening passage, the author of Qustas lays out his plan for the book. Despite the textual corruption, we can extract the key structural and methodological commitments. Let's parse the introduction together to see how the work is organized and what the author prioritizes.

Guided Path
1
Locate the opening formula
The passage begins with the basmala and hamdala. This is standard in Islamic scholarly works, signaling the author's piety and framing the work within a sacred context.
Even with OCR corruption, these phrases are recognizable.
2
Extract the author's stated purpose
The author says he intends a comprehensive work on the laws of logic, drawing from earlier scholars. He highlights noble points and strange objections, aiming for clarity and fairness.
Look for phrases like 'جامع لقوانين المنطق' (comprehensive work on logic laws).
3
Identify the structural division
The book is arranged upon an introduction (مقدمة) and two articles (مقالتين). The first article is on 'forms' (الصور, i.e., concepts/tasawwurat) and the second on 'assents' (التصديقات).
The word 'مقالدين' in the Arabic is likely a scribal error for 'مقالتين'.
4
Clarify the meaning of 'forms'
In this context, 'forms' (الصور) refers to concepts (تصورات), not Platonic Forms. This is the standard division of knowledge into concepts and assents in Islamic logic.
This interpretation is confirmed by the parallel with the second article on assents.
5
Note the author's methodological stance
The author emphasizes fairness and warns against blind imitation. He commits to investigating truth without favoritism, which aligns with the critical spirit of logical inquiry.
Phrases like 'طريق التحقيق مع الإنصاف' (path of investigation with fairness) are key.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

Title and Author: Qustas al-Afkar
Title page identifying the work and author with manuscript date.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author, title, and metaphorical meaning of 'Qustas al-Afkar' as a balance for reasoning.

Core Idea
Logic is the balance that distinguishes truth from falsehood.

Every book begins with its title – a key that unlocks its purpose. 'Qustas al-Afkar fi al-Mantiq' is not just a name; 'Qustas' means a scale or balance, signaling that logic is the instrument for weighing arguments. This lesson orients you to the author, the work, and the metaphor that governs the entire tradition of Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and title
Read the Arabic title: 'قسطاس الأفكار في المنطق لشمس الدين السمرقندي'. The author is Shams al-Din al-Samarqandi, a prominent 13th-century scholar. The book is 'Qustas al-Afkar fi al-Mantiq' (The Balance of Thoughts in Logic).
The manuscript date 930 appears below, likely the Hijri year of this copy.
2
Interpret the metaphor of 'balance'
The word 'Qustas' (قسطاس) means a balance or scale. In Islamic thought, logic is considered the 'balance' for reasoning – a tool to weigh evidence and distinguish sound arguments from fallacious ones. This metaphor connects to Quranic injunctions to use just measure.
This metaphor appears in other works such as al-Ghazali's 'Mi'yar al-'Ilm' (The Standard of Knowledge).
3
Locate the work within the Islamic logical tradition
Al-Samarqandi's Qustas is a concise textbook on logic, used widely in madrasa curricula. It follows the Aristotelian tradition adapted by Muslim logicians, covering definitions, propositions, syllogisms, and dialectic.
Compare with other introductory works like al-Abhari's 'Isaghuji' or al-Katibi's 'Shamsiyya'.

Author states his purpose and method

Learning Objective

Core Idea
This book is not just a summary; it is a critical guide to the logical tradition.

The author opens his work with a clear statement of intent. He is not simply copying earlier works; he is engaging with them, adding his own insights, and judging which views are strongest. Understanding his purpose helps you read the rest of the book with the right expectations.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the opening statement
Find the sentence after 'wa ba'd' that describes the book. Look for active verbs like 'contains' or 'is filled'.

2
Identify the three components
Spot the words for collection (جامع), additions and objections (مشحونة بزيادات واعتراضات), and designation (معيناً لما هو أحرى بالقبول).
These correspond to compilation, critique, and arbitration.
3

What does it mean for the author to designate what is more worthy of acceptance? This shows he is not neutral; he exercises critical judgment.
This is a scholarly stance, not mere transmission.

بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم رب وفق الحمد لله الذي تحيرت العقول في إدراك هويته و اعترفت النهي بكمال ألوهيته، و شهدت الحوادث على وجوب أزليته. و السلام على ذوي الأنفس القدسية و الشيم المرضية؛ خصوصاً على خير البرية و صاحب الآيات البهية محمد و على آله وأصحابه الطاهرين. و بعد فهذا الكتاب جامع لقوانين المنطق أوردنا فيه جملاً وافية و أصولاً كافية من مقالة العلماء المتقدمين و الفضلاء المتأخرين، مشحونة بزيادات شريفة و اعتراضات غريبة، مشيراً إلى مواضع الخلاف، و معيناً لما هو أحرى بالقبول و الاعتراف.
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. O Lord, grant success. Praise be to Allah, whose essence minds are bewildered in comprehending, and intellects acknowledge the perfection of His divinity, and temporal events testify to the necessity of His eternity. And peace be upon those with holy souls and pleasing dispositions; especially upon the best of creation, the possessor of clear signs, Muhammad, and upon his family and his pure Companions. To proceed: This book is a comprehensive collection of the rules of logic. Commentary
This passage is the author's preface (front matter) to his work 'Qustas al-Afkar'. It begins with the basmala, a prayer for divine assistance ('Rabbi waffiq'), and a praise of Allah that highlights the limitations of human intellect in comprehending the divine essence, while affirming that the existence of temporal events proves the necessity of God's eternity. He explains that he has included complete sentences and sufficient principles from both earlier scholars (al-mutaqaddimin) and later virtuous ones (al-muta'akhkhirin), enriched with noble additions (ziyadat sharifa) and unusual objections (i'tiradat ghariba). The author also indicates that he points out points of disagreement (mawadi' al-khilaf) and specifies what is more worthy of acceptance and recognition (ahra bi'l-qabul wa'l-i'tiraf). Thus, the passage sets the stage for a critical and comprehensive work in logic.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Purpose and Structure of Qustas al-Afkar
Author presents the purpose and structure of his logic book Qustas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the purpose and structure of a classical Islamic logic text and explain the fundamental division between tasawwurat (concepts) and tasdiqat (assents).

Core Idea
Knowledge divides into concepts and assents; this shapes all Islamic logic.

This lesson introduces the author's preface to his work Qustas al-Afkar. We will see how he frames the book as a comprehensive collection of logical principles, enriched with additions and objections, and we will understand the key organizational principle: the division between tasawwurat (concepts) and tasdiqat (assents). This bipartite structure is foundational for the entire Islamic logical tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book's title and purpose
Locate the sentence where the author names the book and states its purpose: 'Qustas al-Afkar fi Tahqiq al-Asrar' and 'this book is a comprehensive collection of the rules of logic'.
The title translates to 'The Balance of Thoughts in Investigating Secrets'.
2
Find the structural division
At the end of the preface, the author writes: 'It is arranged into a preface and two articles: the first on concepts (tasawwurat) and the second on assents (tasdiqat).' Note that the preface introduces the work, and the two articles cover the two main branches of knowledge.
3
Define tasawwurat and tasdiqat
Tasawwurat are concepts or notions without judgment (e.g., the meaning of 'sun'). Tasdiqat are assents or judgments that affirm or deny something (e.g., 'the sun is bright'). This distinction is fundamental in Islamic epistemology.
These terms appear in the key_terms list; ensure you understand them.
4
Recognize the author's exhortation to fairness
The author urges the reader to study diligently, avoid fanaticism, and not reject truth out of blind imitation. This reflects the ethical dimension of Islamic scholarship.
The phrase 'God is between me and him' underscores accountability.

بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
رب وفق
الحمد لله الذي تحيرت العقول في إدراك هويته و اعترفت النهي بكمال ألوهيته، و شهدت الحوادث على وجوب أزليته. و السلام على ذوي الأنفس القدسية و الشيم المرضية؛ خصوصاً على خير البرية و صاحب الآيات البهية محمد و على آله وأصحابه الطاهرين. و بعد فهذا الكتاب جامع لقوانين المنطق أوردنا فيه جملاً وافية و أصولاً كافية من مقالة العلماء المتقدمين و الفضلاء المتأخرين، مشحونة بزيادات شريفة و اعتراضات غريبة، مشيراً إلى مواضع الخلاف، و معيناً لما هو أحرى بالقبول و الاعتراف.
و المرجوا تمن سلك محجة الإنصاف و بعد عن طريق الاعتساف أن يمعن في دقائقها و يتأمل في حقائقها، و أن لا يميل إلى جانب تعصباً و لا يرفض جانب الحق تقلداً، و إلا فالله بيني و بینه و کفی به عليماً. و ستميناه قسطاس الأفكار في تحقيق الأسرار و هو مرتب على مقدمة و مقالتين. الأولى: في التصورات و الثانية: في التصديقات.
In the name of God, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Lord, grant success. Praise be to God, Whose intellects are perplexed in grasping His essence, and minds acknowledge the perfection of His divinity, and events bear witness to the necessity of His eternity. And peace be upon those with holy souls and pleasing temperaments; especially upon the best of creation, the possessor of brilliant signs, Muhammad, and upon his family and his pure companions. To proceed: This book is a comprehensive collection of the rules of logic. We have presented in it complete statements and sufficient principles from the discourse of the earlier and later scholars, filled with noble additions and rare objections, pointing to points of disagreement, and indicating what is more worthy of acceptance and recognition. The hope is that whoever follows the path of fairness and distances himself from the way of coercion will delve into its subtleties and contemplate its realities, not leaning toward a side out of fanaticism nor rejecting the side of truth out of blind imitation; otherwise, God is between me and him, and sufficient is He as Knower. And we have named it 'Qustas al-Afkar fi Tahqiq al-Asrar'. It is arranged into a preface and two articles: the first on concepts (tasawwurat) and the second on assents (tasdiqat).
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage is the author's preface to his logic work. It begins with the basmala and praise of God, setting the tone. The author explains the book's purpose: it is a comprehensive collection of logical principles, drawing from both earlier and later scholars. The work is enriched with valuable additions and rare objections, and it points to points of disagreement, indicating which view is more deserving of acceptance. The author then addresses the reader, urging a fair and unbiased study of the work, warning against fanaticism and blind imitation. Finally, he states the title 'Qustas al-Afkar fi Tahqiq al-Asrar' and outlines the structure: a preface and two main articles, the first dealing with concepts (tasawwurat) and the second with assents (tasdiqat). This division reflects the standard classification in Islamic logic, where knowledge is divided into conception and assent.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Distinguishing Tasawwur and Tasdiq in Qustas
Author defines conceptualization and assent and outlines the book's structure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish tasawwur from tasdiq based on the presence or absence of judgment, and identify where each is studied in Qustas.

Core Idea
Logic rests on two pillars: concept without judgment, and assent with judgment.

This opening passage of Qustas al-Afkar establishes the foundational distinction that divides the entire study of logic. The author first urges sincerity and fairness, then reveals the book's title and structure. You will learn to recognize tasawwur and tasdiq as the two fundamental modes of knowledge, and see how the book's division into two treatises mirrors this classification. Mastering this distinction is essential for understanding how logic treats definitions (concepts) and arguments (judgments).

Guided Path
1
Locate the definitions
Find the Arabic words 'التصور' and 'التصديق' in the passage. Read the definitions given: 'العلم إما تصور إن كان إدراكاً بدون الحكم، أو تصديق إن كان معه'. Note that both are species of 'knowledge' (العلم).
The definitions appear at the end of the passage.
2
Identify the differentiating property
The key difference is the presence or absence of judgment (الحكم). Tasawwur is perception without judgment; tasdiq is perception with judgment. For example, understanding the meaning of 'human' is tasawwur, while affirming 'human is rational' is tasdiq.
Judgment here means affirming or denying a predicate of a subject.
3
Relate to the book's structure
Notice the book is divided into two treatises: the first on 'التصورات' (concepts) and the second on 'التصديقات' (assents). This directly reflects the two categories of knowledge. The first treatise deals with definitions, the second with syllogisms.
The introduction includes a chapter on the essence of logic.
4
Apply with an Islamic example
Take the concept 'الصلاة' (prayer). Knowing its meaning (ritual worship with specific actions) is tasawwur. Judging that 'الصلاة واجبة' (prayer is obligatory) is tasdiq. Identify the judgment in a simple fiqh proposition.
This illustrates how the two modes permeate Islamic sciences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخطبة قسطاس الأفكار في المنطق و المرجوا تمن سلك محجة الإنصاف و بعد عن طريق الاعتساف أن يمعن في دقائقها و يتأمل في حقائقها، و أن لا يميل إلى جانب تعصباً و لا يرفض جانب الحق تقلداً، و إلا فالله بيني و بینه و کفی به عليماً. و ستميناه "قسطاس الأفكار في تحقيق الأسرار" و هو مرتب على مقدمة و مقالتين. الأولى: في التصورات و الثانية: في التصديقات. المقدمة الفصل الأوّل في ماهية المنطق و وجه الحاجة إليه التصور و التصديق عند المتأخرين] قالوا: [التصوّر و التصديق] العلم إما تصوّر إن كان إدراكاً بدون الحكم، أو تصديق إن كان معه
The sermon: Qustas al-Afkar fi al-Mantiq. And the hope from whoever follows the path of fairness and stays away from the way of injustice is that he will delve into its subtleties and contemplate its realities, and not incline to a side out of fanaticism nor reject a side of truth out of imitation, otherwise God is between me and him, and sufficient as Knower. And we have named it 'Qustas al-Afkar fi Tahqiq al-Asrar' and it is arranged on an introduction and two treatises: the first on concepts (tasawwurat) and the second on assents (tasdiqat). The introduction: the first chapter on the essence of logic and the need for it. Conceptualization and assent according to the later scholars. They said: Knowledge is either conceptualization if it is perception without judgment, or assent if it is with it.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is the opening of Qustas, serving as both an introduction and a statement of purpose. The author first addresses the reader, urging sincerity and fairness in studying logic, warning against fanaticism and blind imitation. He then reveals the title of the work and its structure: the book is divided into an introduction and two main parts. The first part deals with concepts (tasawwurat) and the second with assents (tasdiqat). The introduction's first chapter explains the essence of logic and why it is needed. The author then defines the two fundamental modes of knowledge according to later scholars: tasawwur is comprehension without judgment, like understanding the meaning of 'human' without affirming or denying anything; tasdiq is comprehension accompanied by judgment, such as affirming that 'four is even'. This classification is foundational to the logical tradition. The student should note that the entire logical enterprise rests on these two categories: logic provides rules for forming correct concepts (definitions) and sound judgments (syllogisms).

Key Terms
التصور
التصديق
المنطق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Tasawwur is perception with judgment, tasdiq without.
B) Tasawwur is perception without judgment, tasdiq with.
C) Both are the same.
D) Tasawwur is of universals only, tasdiq of particulars.

Key Takeaway
Knowledge is divided into concept (without judgment) and assent (with judgment); logic studies both through definitions and syllogisms respectively.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Mapping the Second Article: Acquiring Assents
Author opens the second article on acquiring assents with an outline of its chapters.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the structure and subject matter of the second article of this logic work, distinguishing it from the first article on concepts.

Core Idea
Acquiring assents is the heart of logic's second article, built on concepts.

This passage marks the transition from concepts (tasawwurat) to assents (tasdiqat) in the study of logic. The author announces that the second article will explore how we acquire assents, starting with the first chapter on propositions (qadaya). Understanding this structural division is crucial for navigating the rest of the work and appreciating how logic builds knowledge step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main divisions of knowledge in logic
Recall that logic divides knowledge into concepts (tasawwurat) and assents (tasdiqat). The first article covered concepts; this second article covers assents. Recognise this as a fundamental organising principle.
2
Locate the article announcement in Arabic
Find the phrase 'المقالة الثانية: في اكتساب التصديقات' and note the word 'تصديقات' (assents). This tells you the entire article is devoted to the process of achieving certainty through judgments.
3
Parse the chapter title and its scope
The first chapter is 'في أقسام القضايا وأجزائها وأحكامها' — on the divisions, parts, and rulings of propositions. Understand that propositions are the basic units of assents, and this chapter will break them down.
The chapter has multiple sections (فصول) which will be introduced later.
4
Connect this structure to your own learning path
Realise that just as the first article gave you the building blocks (concepts), this second article will teach you how to combine them into judgments and eventually into proofs. This structural awareness helps you mentally organise the material.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقالة الثانية: فيها أبواب: في اكتساب التصديقات. [الباب] الأول: في أقسام القضايا و أجزائها وأحكامها. و فيه فصول:
The second article: containing chapters: on acquiring assents. The first chapter: on the divisions of propositions and their parts and their rulings. And it contains sections:
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage marks the beginning of the second major article of the work, which focuses on acquiring assents (tasdiqat). The first article covered concepts (tasawwurat). The author announces that this article contains chapters (abwab), the first of which deals with propositions (qadaya): their divisions, constituent parts, and rulings. This structural outline prepares the reader for the detailed logical analysis of propositions that follows.

Key Terms
تصديقات
قضايا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The second article focuses on propositions (qadaya) and their parts, which are the building blocks of assents.
